Mexican mayor Carlos Manzo who spoke against drug gangs assassinated. Who was he?
By
HT News Desk
Updated on: Nov 02, 2025 02:51 pm IST
Manzo was assassinated during an event marking the Day of the Dead, some videos of which have surfaced online.

Mayor of Mexico's Uruapan city, Carlos Manzo, was shot dead during a public event on Saturday (local time), said authorities. The mayor was killed in an attack at the city center, said national public security agency in a statement, reported news agency AFP.
Carlos Manzo became Uruapan's mayor in September 2024(Facebook/Carlos Manzo)
Carlos Manzo became Uruapan's mayor in September 2024(Facebook/Carlos Manzo)

Uruapan is part of Mexico's western state of Michoacan, which has long been troubled by violence and organized crime, according to the report.

Two people were arrested in connection with the assassination and one of the suspects later died, said the public security agency.

Also read: 'Blood everywhere', people shouted 'we love you': Witnesses recall UK train mass stabbing horror
Who was Carlos Manzo?

Mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, was up against drug traffickers in the state of Michoacan, which is crippled with violence by drug cartels, and had made repeated pleas to Mexican President Claudia Sheinbaum for more resources to tackle them, reported the New York Times.

Also read: At least 23 killed, including children, in Mexico supermarket explosion

He was an open critic of Sheinbaum and her approach towards the organised crime in the country and had expressed that he felt threatened for his life lately. While he was a member of Sheinbaum's party Morena in the past, Manzo had ran as an independent in 2024 to become Uruapan's mayor and won.

As mayor, Manzo would occasionally put on a bulletproof vest and and join security patrols on the streets of his city, the AFP report said.

Manzo was assassinated during an event marking the Day of the Dead, some videos of which have surfaced online, purportedly showing people running to safety after gunshots were fired.

Right before the assassination, Manzo had shared a video from the event on his Facebook account. It was around 8 pm when he was shot and later succumbed to his injures at a hospital, the New York Times reported citing Michoacán state's attorney general Carlos Torres Piña. Who was Carlos Manzo? Tributes pour in as Uruapan mayor trends on X following execution
Carlos Manzo, municipal president of City of Uruapan in Mexico, was fatally shot during Festival of Candles on Saturday, November 1. The politician was known for his firm stance against the organized crime-related violence.

The municipal president of Uruapan, Michoacán, Carlos Alberto Manzo Rodríguez, died in the hospital, after being shot this Saturday night while inaugurating the Candle Festival in the main square of that city.

Councilor Víctor Saladitas, a municipal employee, as well as a bodyguard of the mayor were also injured at the scene.

According to the first reports, it was announced that at the beginning of that event and in the midst of thousands of people, two armed men shot at the independent municipal president. When repelling the attack, the security force and police elements injured one of the attackers who apparently died on the way to the hospital and detained another.

Paramedic personnel gave first aid to the victims and took them to a hospital in the city of Uruapan, where Carlos Manzo was reported to be in a very serious condition, with several shots in different parts of the body. The bodyguard is also considered delicate, as well as the councilor Víctor Saladitas, who has three bullet wounds.

Hours before the attack, Manzo Rodríguez toured the main streets of the downtown area, from where he made a live broadcast through his social networks.

The governor of Michoacán, Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, condemned the attack against the municipal president on social networks and reported that security elements are at the scene.

“We strongly condemn the cowardly attack in which the mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, lost his life, for which two people are already detained and one more is dejected. The Secretary of Public Security, Juan Carlos Oseguera Cortés and the National Guard are in the municipality coordinating security actions,” he said.

The case of the murdered mayor in Uruapan, Michoacán, Carlos Manzo, continues to advance and more details are revealed of the moment a man took his life. All, due to some videos of the moment that circulate on social networks.

After the assassination of the municipal president of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, on the night of November 1, The young man who shot him at least seven times was killed on the spot after a struggle with the mayor’s bodyguards..

In the recording you can see how At least eight uniformed officers try to subdue the perpetrator of the attack, pulling him along; Among the shouts of the crowd, a gunshot is heard and the subject falls lying on the grass..

In another of the videos broadcast on social networks, with a duration of 3 minutes and 59 seconds, A person is seen lying on the ground, wearing black pants and a white sweater, surrounded by at least four bodyguards; A man approaches and asks, “He went, didn’t he?” and one of the mayor’s guards responds: “Yes, this was it, yes, the son of a bitch ran to the side…”.

In that same recording, another person asks him: “Who sent you, son of your…”, however, the aggressor does not make any sound, only that he is breathing..
What is being investigated in the Carlos Manzo case?

Yesterday, the Secretary of Security and Citizen Protection, Omar García Harfuch pointed out that no line of investigation will be ruled out, although so far the motive points to organized crime, and not an attack motivated by political reasons..
Lee: Despite security reinforcements, homicides continue in Michoacán

“Right now the expert reports and statements are progressing in the local prosecutor’s office. Yesterday I spoke with the Attorney General of the Republic and today we will have another assessment. In due course, the prosecutor himself will inform whether the case will be attracted or not. But what we have at the moment is organized crime,” he said.

García Harfuch emphasized that the Attorney General’s Office (FGR) maintains autonomy in its decisions, although there is constant coordination with the federal government.

Thousands protest against government in Mexico as clashes leave 120 injured
2 days ago
Ruth Comerford and
Ethirajan Anbarasan,Global Affairs reporter
Watch: Protesters against violent crime and the Sheinbaum government clash with police in Mexico City

At least 120 people - 100 of them police officers - have been injured in clashes during anti-government protests in Mexico City, police said.

Thousands of demonstrators marched in the Mexican capital on Saturday to protest against violent crime and President Claudia Sheinbaum's government.

Sheinbaum said the marches, which also took place in other cities, had been funded by right-wing politicians who oppose her government.

The rally was organised by Gen Z youth groups, drawing support from citizens protesting against high-profile killings, including the assassination just weeks ago of Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo - who had called for tough action against cartels.

Demonstrators dismantled parts of a barrier protecting the National Palace, where Sheinbaum lives. Police protecting the compound used tear gas on the crowds.

Authorities have arrested 20 people for crimes including robbery and assault, Mexico City security chief Pablo Vazquez told reporters.

Protesters waved banners displaying messages including "We are all Carlos Manzo", while others wore cowboy hats in tribute to him.
EPA A protester wearing a gasmask and mustard-coloured gloves holds up a fence during a demonstration near the National Palace in Mexico. EPA

Manzo was shot on 1 November while he attended a Day of the Dead festival.

He was known for speaking openly about drug-trafficking gangs in his town and cartel violence.

He had been demanding tough action against armed cartel members who terrorise the country.

Sheinbaum has been acting against cartels but resisting calls for another all-out war on drugs. Previous attempts by her predecessors have ended with bloody results.

Days before the march took place, the president said the demonstration was being promoted by bots online.

"We agree with freedom of expression and freedom of demonstration if there are young people who have demands, but the issue here is who is promoting the demonstration," she said in a briefing.

"People should know how this demonstration was organised so that no one is used."
Reuters Thousands turned out on the streets of Mexico City to protest against insecurity and corruption in the country. Reuters
Some protesters paid tribute to Uruapan mayor Carlos Manzo

Sheinbaum retains approval ratings above 70% in her first year in office, and has made in-roads in clamping down on fentanyl-trafficking – a key issue for her US counterpart, Donald Trump.

But she has been criticised for failing to halt the violence gripping the country and is facing increased hostility from nearby countries.

Earlier this month, Peru's Congress voted to declare Sheinbaum a persona non grata - or unwelcome in the country.

The decision came days after Peru severed diplomatic ties with Mexico, after the Mexican government granted asylum to a former Peruvian prime minister facing charges for a 2022 coup attempt.
Quién era Carlos Manzo, el alcalde asesinado en México que le había pedido al gobierno de Sheinbaum apoyo para enfrentar al crimen organizado

Información del artículo

        Autor, Santiago VanegasSantiago Vanegas

    Título del autor, BBC News Mundo

    Autor, Daniel PardoDaniel Pardo

        Título del autor, Corresponsal de BBC News Mundo en México
    3 noviembre 2025

El asesinato del alcalde de Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, durante una celebración de Día de Muertos ha provocado una ola de rechazo y cuestionamientos contra el gobierno federal.

Manzo falleció este sábado tras recibir varios disparos en una plaza pública del centro de la ciudad durante el tradicional Festival de las Velas.

De 40 años, se había convertido en el primer alcalde independiente en la historia del municipio, tras ganar las elecciones locales de 2024. Se hacía llamar "el del sombrero".

Desde la campaña a la presidencia municipal, se hizo conocido por su discurso de mano dura contra el crimen organizado.

Sus declaraciones, a menudo controversiales, lo habían vuelto popular en redes sociales, incluso por fuera de su municipio.

En mayo, por ejemplo, se dirigió a la policía municipal diciendo: "Delincuente que se topen que ande armado, y que se resista a ser detenido o que agreda a la ciudadanía y ustedes los detecten en la calle o en los operativos, hay que abatirlos".

"No hay que tener ninguna consideración con ellos", agregó.

En su momento, la presidenta Sheinbaum rechazó las declaraciones de Manzo.

Final de Más leídas

El fallecido alcalde también le dijo a un grupo de mujeres de su ciudad que, si sus hijos estaban metidos en el crimen, "no anden chillando si al rato se los mata el gobierno en un enfrentamiento".

Antes de ser alcalde, Manzo había sido legislador por el partido de Sheinbaum, Morena, del que luego se distanció y contra el cual se enfrentó en las elecciones en Uruapan de 2024.

Fin de WhatsApp

Tras conocerse la noticia de su muerte, recirculó una publicación de Facebook en la que Manzo les pedía a la presidenta Claudia Sheinbaum y al secretario de Seguridad, Omar García Harfuch, "que no dejen solo a Uruapan en el combate de los delitos federales que le corresponde a la Federación atender".

En su mensaje, Manzo criticaba que se hubiera retirado a 200 elementos de la guardia nacional del municipio: "Esta decisión deja a Uruapan en estado vulnerable ante las actividades ilícitas del crimen organizado", señaló hace menos de un mes.

El alcalde había recientemente cancelado las fiestas patrias en su municipio por los riesgos de seguridad y en videos se le veía usando un chaleco antibalas.

Algunos ciudadanos han criticado que el gobierno federal no hiciera más para proteger su seguridad.

En su conferencia de prensa de este lunes, la presidenta Claudia Sheinbaum señaló que se le había estado brindando a Uruapan el apoyo que Manzo había solicitado.

La mandataria también condenó el homicidio, ofreció sus condolencias a la familia y se comprometió a que no haya impunidad en el caso.

El secretario de Seguridad, Omar García Harfuch, señaló por su parte que los delincuentes aprovecharon que el alcalde se encontraba en un evento público en el que no había controles para ingresar.

Las autoridades abatieron a uno de los presuntos agresores y detuvieron a otros dos después de los hechos, según informó el gabinete de Seguridad.

Las reacciones en redes sociales de los seguidores de Manzo resaltan su lucha contra el crimen organizado y lo catalogan como un líder nacional.

Su cuenta de Facebook cuenta con cerca de 1 millón de seguidores, a pesar de que la población del municipio de Uruapan no excede los 400.000 habitantes.

Cientos de personas se reunieron frente al palacio de gobierno en Morelia, la capital del estado de Michoacán, para rechazar el homicidio del alcalde y pedir justicia. Algunos, inclusive, pedían la renuncia de la presidenta Claudia Sheinbaum
Un hombre sostiene un letrero rojo con un mensaje que reclama justicia en una manifestación.

Fuente de la imagen, EPA/Shutterstock
Pie de foto, Frente al palacio municipal de Morelia, se presentaron protestas este domingo.
Un alcalde especial

Análisis de Daniel Pardo, corresponsal en México de BBC Mundo

El asesinato de Manzo pudo haber pasado como otro más de un alcalde en México: este año, ya se registran al menos 10 casos similares.

Sin embargo, la muerte de Manzo ha generado una repercusión especial.

Primero, por el perfil de la víctima: de carisma frentero y cercano, siempre con sombrero de ala ancha, Manzo, que rondaba los 40 años, lanzó una ambiciosa campaña en contra del poder del crimen organizado.

Él mismo se declaró consciente de los riesgos que su campaña implicaba: "No quiero ser otro presidente municipal más de la lista de los ejecutados", dijo una vez, y "si decir la verdad me cuesta la vida, que me la cobren caro", dijo otra.

Al perfil de Manzo se suma el hecho de que el gobierno de Sheinbaum también puso la Seguridad como prioridad y de manera constante reporta cifras de disminución de la violencia en el país. Casos como éste, entonces, alientan a la oposición a decir que los resultados de Sheinbaum no son ciertos.

Por último, está el factor espacial: Michoacán, al articular tres regiones distintas de México, es un epicentro de la disputa entre carteles, en parte por su riqueza agrícola. Allí recientemente se encontró otro centro de reclutamiento del narco. Y se trata de una sociedad con una larga tradición de resistencia y movilización.

Y eso, también, es otra razón para pensar que la muerte de Manzo dará mucho más de qué hablar.


Mexican church leaders demand action after mayor Carlos Manzo murdered at Day of the Dead ceremony
By
OSV News -
4 November 2025, 13:24 78
Mayor Carlos Manzo of Uruapan, Mexico, one of the few independent politicians elected to office in Mexico, attends a candlelight Day of the Dead festival in Uruapan in Michoacán state Nov. 1, 2025, shortly before he was shot dead. (OSV News screenshot Carlos Manzo via Facebook handout via Reuters) THIS IMAGE HAS BEEN SUPPLIED BY A THIRD PARTY. MANDATORY CREDIT. NO RESALES. NO ARCHIVES. VERIFICATION: Reuters was able to confirm the location and date of the footage by reports of local authorities.

The Mexican bishops’ conference has condemned the murder of a mayor, who was assassinated after pleading for federal assistance in combating drug cartels — which extort avocado growers in his municipality in western Michoacán state.

Carlos Manzo, the mayor of Uruapan, was shot dead at a candlelighting ceremony for Day of the Dead on Nov. 1. Manzo was shot seven times, according to Mexico’s public security secretary, Omar García Harfuch, while photos from the event in the town square showed him holding his young son in his arms. Two suspects were arrested in the case, García Harfuch added.

Manzo’s slaying “adds to a series of murders of people who have dared to speak out and confront the absence of the rule of law in their communities, businesses and other spaces. Today, it is no longer enough to apprehend the killer: We must resolutely combat the root causes of all these murders,” the bishops’ conference said in a Nov. 2 statement.

“The ordinary presence of armed groups, which control the public life of citizens in various regions of the country, is the real crime to be faced: the roadblocks, the dispossession of lands, the constant threats to producers, merchants and rulers reflect a serious weakening of the constitutional order that the governments at the municipal, state and federal levels, are obligated to guarantee.”
Riot police officers detain a woman during a demonstration in Morelia, Mexico, Nov. 2, 2025, over the assassination of Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo. Manzo was assassinated Nov. 1 in a plaza in front of dozens of people who had gathered for Day of the Dead festivities, authorities said. (OSV News photo/Asaid Castro, Reuters)

The brazen murder sparked outrage in Mexico, where drug cartel violence has plagued swaths of the country for nearly two decades. The violence has especially plagued Michoacán, which has a long history of marijuana growing. But analysts say that now criminal groups now extort the growers of avocados and limes, illegally log forests and import chemical precursors for synthetic drugs through the port of Lázaro Cárdenas.

A priest in Michoacán described a desperate situation in the state with criminal groups colluding with politicians and fighting each other to control lucrative crime territories.

“The people are saying, ‘Enough, padre,” the priest, who ministers in a conflictive part of Michoacán, told OSV News. The priest, who previously lent spiritual support to self-defense groups that formed to fight drug cartels in 2013, asked for anonymity to speak candidly. “Believe me: We’re just a minute, a moment away from Michoacán burning,” the priest said.

Manzo became known for accompanying police as they patrolled Uruapan. He spoke out against organized crime and urged President Claudia Sheinbaum to take action.

“This country has already slipped out of the president’s control,” Manzo told Mexican media outlet Latinus. “The country is slipping away from us. Crime has become part of the landscape. … We are facing crime alone. There is no strategy, there is no state.”

Confronting criminal groups can be perilous. Bernardo Bravo, head of a citrus growers’ association in the city of Apatzingán, was recently found murdered after he organized a protest by citrus growers tired of paying extortion.
Riot police detain a man during a demonstration in Morelia, Mexico, Nov. 2, 2025, over the assassination of Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo. Manzo was assassinated Nov. 1 in a plaza in front of dozens of people who had gathered for Day of the Dead festivities, authorities said. (OSV News photo/Ivan Arias, Reuters)

“These crimes wound Mexican society and demand an immediate and coordinated response from the authorities to rebuild peace in Michoacán,” said a Nov. 2 statement from the National Dialogue for Peace, an initiative to pacify Mexico, sponsored by the bishops’ conference, the Jesuits and the Conference of Religious Superiors of Mexico.

Sheinbaum condemned the killing of Manzo, who previously served in Congress as a member of her ruling Morena party and won the mayor’s office as an independent. She drew controversy on Nov. 3, however, for saying at her morning press conference that violence in Michoacán originated with former President Felipe Calderón — who she insisted stole the 2006 election and started cracking down on drug cartels in Michoacán to “legitimize” his win.

“And we have always said it is about addressing the causes and zero impunity, intelligence, investigation and prosecutions,” Sheinbaum said.

Calderón’s crackdown on drug cartels shortly followed his taking office in December 2006. It was preceded by a drug cartel known as La Familia Michoacana bursting into a bar in Uruapan and tossing five human heads onto a dance floor.

Manzo’s murder captured international attention and came as U.S. pressure on Mexico to stop the flow of drugs like fentanyl has mounted.

“The U.S. stands ready to deepen security cooperation with Mexico to wipe out organized crime on both sides of the border,” Christopher Landau, deputy secretary of state, said on X. “May his soul rest in peace and may his memory inspire prompt and effective action.”
The case of the murdered mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, continues to move and it was recently announced that the city council itself is preparing a tribute for the politician. What is it about?

The Municipal Government of Uruapan invited the population to donate keys to create a monument in honor of Carlos Alberto Manzo Rodríguezmunicipal president of this city, who was assassinated on November 1 when the Candle Festival was inaugurated.

Through its social networks, the government announced the “Not one step back” campaign and informed the population that The keys will be received at the offices of the House of Culture, located in the Historic Center, in front of the Municipal Pergola.

Review Why does the mayor of Uruapan ask for a punishment vote in 2027?

“Each key you give is a symbol of love, gratitude and hope. From Uruapan hands will be born the monument that will forever remember a man who dedicated his life to serving, to building, to dreaming of a more just and humane Uruapan. Let’s forge his legacy together”.
“Don’t leave me alone”

Yesterday, Grecia Quiroz García left the house of culture with her husband’s hat in her hand and went on stage under a strong security device. The independent mayor was flanked by her escorts dressed in suits, by elements of the National Guard and the Army, and by her family.

With her gaze fixed on two paintings of her husband, she said: “Today, at this moment, Carlos Manzo is standing here next to me, and I want to tell you that This fight will not be in vain. “They may have taken away our leader, but they left us a hero for whom we are going to fight and honor his memory.”.
Lee: Very cold days are coming for Guadalajara; This is how it will be today Saturday

Amongst applause, the new mayor of that municipality located 110 kilometers from the capital of Michoacán, who was wearing a combination of black and white, stated that Today one of Carlos Manzo’s legacies is fulfilled: seeing his people united by this fight, which he defended until the last day of his life..

Grecia, who at times seemed fearful, changed her mood when she heard from the thousands of attendees who accompanied her, the cry of “You are not alone”.

“Today I come to tell you that there is hope for Uruapan, for Michoacán, for Mexico; for all those people who have lost a loved one, for all those who have been extorted, robbed, abused. Today I want to give you that message of hope.”.
Consultation: Experts warn that very cold days are coming for Guadalajara

Quiroz García recalled that the day a 17-year-old teenager shot her husband, she could only pick up his hat from the floor.. “But those who ordered Carlos Manzo to be killed did not know that this hat has an unstoppable and tireless force. Today I also come to tell you that they would have to come and kill us all so that this fight stops walking in the streets and stops supporting the most vulnerable people.”

As the seconds passed, the mayor’s words rose in tone in that unread message for her people, for the political class and for criminals.
“We are not going to let anyone come to trample on the people of Uruguay.”. We are not going to let anyone come and bloody the people of Uruguay even more, we are not going to allow it. Let’s continue walking with the independent movement of the hat. “I need your help, I need you not to leave me alone.”.
Carlos Manzo talked about not becoming another Mexican mayor who gets executed months before being killed at Day of the Dead event
Mexican mayor Carlos Manzo was killed in a shooting, on Saturday.
posted by Aaratrika Bal
Monday 11/3/2025 at 2:05PM EST


The case of Carlos Manzo has mobilized security corporations to provide projection to the inhabitants of Uruapan and his widow and new mayor, Grecia Quiroz; and this is the position of the federal government:

After the first security cabinet held in Uruapan after the assassination of municipal president Carlos Manzo, and as part of the presentation of the Michoacán Plan, President Claudia Sheinbaum Pardo assured that the Government of Mexico will provide all support to the municipality and its acting mayor, Grecia Quiroz..

During his morning conference, The President explained that both the Secretary of National Defense, Ricardo Trevilla Trejo, and the Secretary of Security and Citizen Protection, Omar García Harfuch, carried out a work tour that began in Morelia and concluded in Uruapanwhere they held meetings with municipal presidents, businessmen and representatives of civil society.

Consultation: How does Grecia Quiroz, mayor of Uruapan, face the dangers?

According to Sheinbaum, In Uruapan, federal officials met with Mayor Grecia Quiroz and businessmen from the region, with whom agreements were established to strengthen security efforts.
Among the commitments assumed are:

    Maintain and reinforce the operations that are already active in Michoacán and
    Coordinate meetings every 15 days, either in Uruapan or Mexico City, to provide timely follow-up on the situation in the municipality.
    Also address the specific needs of Uruapan and the rest of the Michoacán municipalities as part of the Michoacán Plan for Peace and Justice

Sheinbaum reiterated that his government will remain close to local authorities: “Our support is important, both in security issues and in the needs of Uruapan and all the municipalities of Michoacán. We will continue to be present,” he stated.

The president pointed out that some additional points presented by authorities and businessmen will be detailed later by those involved, but insisted that the priority of the Government of Mexico is to accompany the region after the crime that shocked the state.
Grecia Quiroz received threats

Yesterday, the mayor of Uruapan, Grecia Quiroz García, revealed that one day before taking office she received threats, like other officialswhich sought to destabilize his government.
At a press conference, he said that he gives his vote of confidence to the Michoacán Plan for Peace and Justice, and stressed that Mexico needs to know who the intellectual authors of the murder of Carlos Manzo are.

Photograph provided by the Government of Michoacán, of the mayor of Uruapan, Grecia Quiroz (2-d), the governor of the entity, Alfredo Ramírez (3-d), the head of the Secretariat of Security and Citizen Protection, Omar Gracia Harfuch (c), the Secretary of Defense of Mexico, Ricardo Trevilla Trejo (3-d), and the Head of the Office of the Presidency of the Republic, Lázaro Cárdenas (2-d), during a conference press conference in the city of Uruapan (Mexico). The Government of Mexico began an offensive against at least twelve drug trafficking cartels operating in the western state of Michoacán, where in the last month the mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, and the leader of citrus producers, Bernardo Bravo, were murdered. EFE/Government of Michoacán
Carlos Alberto Manzo Rodríguez (Uruapan, 9 de abril de 1985-Uruapan, 1 de noviembre de 2025)[1]​ fue un político mexicano, presidente municipal de Uruapan como candidato independiente del 1 de septiembre de 2024 hasta su asesinato, el 1 de noviembre de 2025. También fue diputado federal en la LXV Legislatura del Congreso de la Unión.[2]​
Primeros años

Carlos Alberto Manzo Rodríguez, nació el 9 de abril de 1985 en Uruapan, Michoacán.[3]​[4]​[5]​ Fue hijo de Juan Manzo Ceja, un activista social de la misma ciudad. Estudió la licenciatura en Ciencias Políticas y Gestión Pública en el Instituto Tecnológico y de Estudios Superiores de Occidente (ITESO). De 2017 a 2018 trabajó como auditor del Instituto Mexicano del Seguro Social (IMSS).[6]​
Diputado federal

En las elecciones federales de 2021 fue postulado por el partido Morena como diputado federal por el distrito 9 de Michoacán, con cabecera en Uruapan. Ocupó el escaño en la LXV Legislatura del Congreso de la Unión del 1 de septiembre de 2021 al 27 de febrero de 2024.[7]​ El 25 de noviembre de 2023 fue detenido brevemente por elementos de la Guardia Civil de Michoacán luego de que el diputado acusara a los policías de intentar extorsionar a una ciudadana. El incidente, transmitido en vivo a través de Facebook, culminó con la liberación de Manzo minutos después.[8]​ El 27 de febrero de 2024 solicitó licencia a su cargo para contender como candidato a la presidencia municipal de Uruapan.[9]​
Presidente municipal de Uruapan

En las elecciones estatales de 2024 se presentó como candidato independiente a la presidencia municipal de Uruapan. Resultó electo con aproximadamente el 66 % de los votos emitidos, convirtiéndose en el primer alcalde independiente del municipio.[10]​

Su administración se caracterizó por su postura crítica hacia la delincuencia y su llamado a medidas contundentes para detener la violencia en la región. Manzo llegó a declarar que «delincuente que se tope que ande armado y que se resista a ser detenido o que agreda a la ciudadanía, hay que abatirlo».[11]​ Esta retórica lo llevó a confrontaciones con el gobernador Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla y la presidenta Claudia Sheinbaum, defensores de la política de seguridad federal «Abrazos, no balazos»; en mayo de 2025, Manzo desafió públicamente a Sheinbaum a demostrar que dicha estrategia podía reducir la criminalidad en Uruapan.[12]​

En septiembre de 2025, tras el asesinato de un policía municipal, Carlos Manzo canceló las festividades del Grito de Independencia y solicitó el apoyo directo de la presidenta Sheinbaum para contener la violencia, argumentando que los grupos delictivos operaban con armas de uso exclusivo del Ejército.[13]​
Asesinato
Plaza Morelos en 2020, lugar dónde Manzo fue asesinado.
Carlos Manzo (encerrado en azul) tras recibir 8 disparos del tirador, Víctor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales (encerrado en rojo).

Carlos Manzo fue asesinado la noche del 1 de noviembre de 2025 en la Plaza Morelos de Uruapan, durante el Festival de las Velas. El alcalde se encontraba tomándose fotografías con un grupo de niños cuando un individuo le disparó en ocho ocasiones, impactándolo en el abdomen y el brazo.[14]​ Un regidor y un escolta también resultaron heridos. El atacante fue abatido en el lugar por el equipo de seguridad de Manzo. El alcalde fue trasladado de urgencia a un hospital local, donde su deceso fue confirmado horas después por el gobernador Ramírez Bedolla.[15]​ El 3 de noviembre, fue sepultado en el Panteón Municipal de San Juan Evangelista.[16]​[17]​

El 6 de noviembre de 2025, la Fiscalía General de Michoacán obtuvo la identidad del asesino, Víctor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales, un adolescente de 17 años, originario de Paracho, quien también estaría correlacionado con el CJNG y cuya acción habrían sido una represalia por la detención de René Belmonte "El Rino".[18]​[19]​[20]​
Respuesta gubernamental

La concejal Hilda Flor del Campo Maldonado Medina fue nombrada sucesora interina de Manzo, mientras que sus partidarios solicitaban que su viuda, Grecia Quiroz, fuera designada para completar su mandato. El gobernador de Michoacán, Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, confirmó que el reemplazo de Manzo sería determinado por su propio movimiento independiente, y se presentó una propuesta formal al respecto ante el Congreso estatal. Quiroz juró como presidenta municipal el 5 de noviembre de 2025, para completar el resto del mandato de su esposo. Prometió continuar con su postura contra el crimen organizado.[21]​[22]​[23]​[24]​

Quiroz se reunió con la presidenta Sheinbaum en Palacio Nacional, Ciudad de México, el 3 de noviembre. Al día siguiente, Sheinbaum anunció el “Plan Michoacán de Paz y Justicia”, un plan de seguridad para el estado que incluye el despliegue de la Guardia Nacional, mayor personal federal y la creación de una unidad especial en la Fiscalía General del Estado. El plan abarca tres grandes áreas temáticas: seguridad y justicia, desarrollo económico con justicia, y educación y cultura para la paz. Se celebrarán reuniones con el gabinete de seguridad federal cada dos semanas y se implementará un sistema de alerta para los alcaldes del estado.[22]​[25]​[26]​
Reacciones públicas

Manzo fue el séptimo presidente municipal asesinado en Michoacán durante la gobernación de Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla y el séptimo presidente municipal asesinado en el país en el 2025.[27]​[28]​

En el funeral de Manzo en Uruapan, el 2 de noviembre, el gobernador Ramírez Bedolla fue recibido con indignación por una multitud de cientos de habitantes. La gente lo tildó de asesino y exigió justicia por el asesinato del alcalde. Su equipo de seguridad le recomendó retirarse tras menos de cinco minutos en la funeraria. Miles de personas marcharon por las calles de Uruapan para acompañar el féretro de Manzo hasta su última morada. Dirigiéndose a la multitud en la plaza principal de la ciudad.[29]​[30]​

Ese mismo día, se organizó una marcha de protesta en Morelia. Posteriormente, un contingente de cientos de personas irrumpió en el Palacio de Gobierno estatal con bombas molotov, palos y piedras, forzaron la entrada principal del edificio y accedieron a las oficinas gubernamentales. Prendieron fuego a algunos muebles, arrojaron otros a la calle y pintaron consignas en las paredes interiores y exteriores. La policía lanzó gases lacrimógenos dentro del complejo para dispersar a los manifestantes, y el edificio quedó bajo custodia policial; ocho personas fueron detenidas.[31]​[32]​[33]​[34]​
Manifestantes de la marcha de Carlos Manzo frente a la presidencia de Zitácuaro.
Duración: 29 segundos.0:29
Marcha de Carlos Manzo cercana al centro de Zitácuaro.

Una segunda marcha en Morelia, organizada por estudiantes el 3 de noviembre, tuvo lugar durante la cual un estudiante de derecho resultó herido en el ojo por una bala de goma. Posteriormente, se realizaron manifestaciones en los municipios michoacanos de Pátzcuaro, Zitácuaro y Apatzingán, con nuevas protestas que condenaban el asesinato de Bernardo Bravo, ocurrido dos semanas antes. En Apatzingán, la cuarta ciudad más grande del estado, los manifestantes irrumpieron en el palacio municipal y prendieron fuego a los muebles. Grecia Quiroz exhortó a la población a evitar manifestaciones violentas, afirmando que no era lo que su esposo hubiera querido.[35]​[36]​[37]​

El 7 de noviembre de 2025 al menos 70 mil personas realizaron una marcha de forma pacífica en la ciudad de Uruapan, en donde también hubo paro general de actividades. Los manifestantes iban vestidos de blanco y con sombrero, exigiendo seguridad para la ciudad y justicia para Carlos Manzo.[38]​[39]​ Asi mismo, la Banda Perla de Michoacán propuso renombrar la canción "Ilusión 98", como un homenaje póstumo.[40]​ 

CIUDAD DE MÉXICO (AP) — Un joven de 17 años fue el autor del asesinato de un alcalde del estado de Michoacán, en el occidente de México, que ha conmocionado al país y desatado protestas en esa región, anunciaron el jueves las autoridades.

A cinco días de la ejecución del político Carlos Manzo, alcalde de la ciudad de Uruapan, el fiscal de Michoacán, Carlos Torres Piña, informó que el autor del crimen fue identificado por sus familiares como Víctor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales.

Manzo, de 40 años, murió la noche del sábado en un hospital de Uruapan tras recibir siete impactos de bala que le realizó un pistolero que lo atacó en una plaza de esa ciudad en medio de decenas de personas que participaban en las celebraciones del Día de Muertos. El agresor falleció en la plaza tras ser tiroteado por la seguridad del alcalde.

Torres Piña expresó en conferencia de prensa que de acuerdo con los estudios se determinó que el atacante tenía “adicciones a la metanfetamina”, lo que fue ratificado por sus familiares quienes reclamaron el cuerpo del joven.

Las investigaciones adelantadas por las autoridades de Michoacán permitieron determinar que en el letal ataque a Manzo participaron “más de dos personas” y que el homicidio está relacionado con “el crimen organizado”, indicó el fiscal estatal.

En los últimos tres años han sido asesinados siete alcaldes en Michoacán, donde ha recrudecido la violencia por la pugna que mantienen varias organizaciones criminales por el control de la región. En Michoacán, que es el principal productor de aguacate y limón del país, operan células del Cártel Jalisco Nueva Generación, la Familia Michoacana y las organizaciones locales Los Viagras, Los Caballeros Templarios y Los Blancos de Troya.

Manzo contaba desde diciembre de 2024 —tres meses después de asumir el cargo— con protección y en mayo se había reforzado su seguridad con personal de la policía municipal y 14 efectivos de la Guardia Nacional.

La identificación del agresor se produjo un día después de que la viuda del alcalde, Grecia Quiroz, asumió como presidenta municipal de Uruapan en reemplazo de su esposo asesinado.

La muerte de Manzo desató protestas en los últimos días en la ciudad de Morelia, capital de Michoacán, Uruapan y Apatzingán, donde el 19 de octubre fue tiroteado el dirigente de los productores de limón de esa región Bernardo Bravo.
CIUDAD DE MÉXICO (AP) — Un joven de 17 años fue el autor del asesinato de un alcalde del estado de Michoacán, en el occidente de México, que ha conmocionado al país y desatado protestas en esa región, anunciaron el jueves las autoridades.

A cinco días de la ejecución del político Carlos Manzo, alcalde de la ciudad de Uruapan, el fiscal de Michoacán, Carlos Torres Piña, informó que el autor del crimen fue identificado por sus familiares como Víctor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales.

Manzo, de 40 años, murió la noche del sábado en un hospital de Uruapan tras recibir siete impactos de bala que le realizó un pistolero que lo atacó en una plaza de esa ciudad en medio de decenas de personas que participaban en las celebraciones del Día de Muertos. El agresor falleció en la plaza tras ser tiroteado por la seguridad del alcalde.

Torres Piña expresó en conferencia de prensa que de acuerdo con los estudios se determinó que el atacante tenía “adicciones a la metanfetamina”, lo que fue ratificado por sus familiares quienes reclamaron el cuerpo del joven.

Las investigaciones adelantadas por las autoridades de Michoacán permitieron determinar que en el letal ataque a Manzo participaron “más de dos personas” y que el homicidio está relacionado con “el crimen organizado”, indicó el fiscal estatal.

Sheinbaum descarta cambios en seguridad tras el asesinato de un alcalde en el occidente de México
Sheinbaum descarta cambios en seguridad tras el asesinato de un alcalde en el occidente de México

En los últimos tres años han sido asesinados siete alcaldes en Michoacán, donde ha recrudecido la violencia por la pugna que mantienen varias organizaciones criminales por el control de la región. En Michoacán, que es el principal productor de aguacate y limón del país, operan células del Cártel Jalisco Nueva Generación, la Familia Michoacana y las organizaciones locales Los Viagras, Los Caballeros Templarios y Los Blancos de Troya.

Manzo contaba desde diciembre de 2024 —tres meses después de asumir el cargo— con protección y en mayo se había reforzado su seguridad con personal de la policía municipal y 14 efectivos de la Guardia Nacional.

La identificación del agresor se produjo un día después de que la viuda del alcalde, Grecia Quiroz, asumió como presidenta municipal de Uruapan en reemplazo de su esposo asesinado.

La muerte de Manzo desató protestas en los últimos días en la ciudad de Morelia, capital de Michoacán, Uruapan y Apatzingán, donde el 19 de octubre fue tiroteado el dirigente de los productores de limón de esa región Bernardo Bravo.

In an interview with “Los Periodistas”, the Undersecretary of the Government of Michoacán, Juan Manzo, assured that the death of his brother, Carlos Manzo, caused deep social consternation not only in the state, but at the national level, for which he asked not to use the case for partisan purposes.

Mexico City, November 7 (However).- Juan ManzoUndersecretary of the Government of Michoacanassured that his brother, Carlos Manzo murdered on November 1, “He was a man related to the leftnot to the right”, despite the attempts of different parties to add him to their ranks.

    “He was an important political actor, attractive based on the weakness of these parties; obviously having a candidate like Carlos was very attractive and the truth is that both the PAN and the PRI, as the Citizen Movement, were looking for him in the idea that he could be a candidate for one of these political forces. But his main essence and the profile of his voters were related to the left,” he said in an interview with Alejandro Páez and Álvaro Delgado for the program “The Journalists” which is broadcast through the YouTube channel of However On Air.

The official explained that the death of Carlos Manzo caused deep social consternation not only in Michoacán, but at the national level, which is why he asked not to use the case for partisan purposes.

“In the midst of the indignation there are many interests that mix to amplify that indignation, some are legitimate, others not properly, perhaps they will be able to share the indignation. I believe that the problem of violence is generalized, but we must avoid that. I would like more for those who speak for the Hat Movement to be those who were there, Carlos’s friends who decided to participate without parties, who decided to gather signatures to achieve independent candidacies in Uruapan, who ran the campaign and finally won resoundingly in the campaign of the year past,” said the state official.

Amid the commotion over the murder of the Mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, the call for the so-called “Generation Z March” began to circulate on social networks, a movement that presents itself as a citizen, but whose promotion on digital platforms and without a visible figure to lead, has raised doubts about its authenticity.

Meanwhile, from the federal government, President Claudia Sheinbaum warned that behind both actions – the use of crime and youth mobilization – lies an attempt by the right to reposition itself politically.

Although the call insists that it has no relationship with any party or economic group, the lack of a visible group or faces that officially promote this movement has generated suspicions about who is behind them and whether they have the support of businessmen or right-wing groups. Among the young people who have promoted the mobilization, Miguel Samaniego, son of Xóchitl Gálvez, former PRIAN presidential candidate, stands out.

Meanwhile, the opposition reacted harshly and immediately. The PAN, the PRI and MC accused the federal government of having left Manzo alone, despite his repeated complaints about the presence of organized crime in Michoacán.

The PAN stated on its social networks that “the fear that Mexican families live with cannot continue.” “The Government must assume its responsibility and guarantee the safety of everyone,” he added. “From the National Executive Committee of the PAN we demand justice, and that peace and tranquility be returned to Michoacán and all of Mexico,” reads its position.

The PRI pointed out that “murdering an elected authority is a direct attack on the Mexican State and another example of the violence that continues to hit our country.”

In this regard, Juan Manzo described these actions as “politicking” and stressed that the important thing at this time is to clarify the murder of his brother.

    “I would not like us to dedicate this space to politicking. Carlos’ death brings great social consternation derived from fatigue, but it is not the result of the violence of this government. Those of us from Uruapan know that violence has been permeated in our society for many years,” said the Michoacan official.

Juan Manzo highlighted that insecurity in Michoacán is not recent, but rather a phenomenon that has been consolidated over the last three decades. “There has been the presence of gangs and later cartels. Uruapan is no exception; on the contrary, it is a very attractive financial and economic bastion for these groups,” he said.

The Undersecretary considered that all lines of investigation must be exhausted to clarify the homicide and determine responsibilities, including those related to the security personnel assigned to the Mayor.

“We ask that an investigation be made into why the escort failed, that this crime be clarified and everyone be investigated. That is a request that comes from society, not from political actors,” he insisted.

Regarding the accusations that some opposition groups have made against Governor Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, the official stated that there was a good relationship between the state president and the Mayor.

    “I am a witness that there was a good relationship between Carlos and the Governor; those are boasts of politicking,” he assured.


The brother of the murdered Mayor also highlighted that Carlos Manzo had political adversaries and confrontations with different local actors, due to his media personality and the accusations he made publicly.

Finally, Juan Manzo asked that those who lead the expressions of protest against the crime be the members of the Sombrero Movement, a group founded by the Mayor and made up of young people and residents of Uruapan.

    “They have the legitimacy to speak and demand justice, not other actors who may not even know them,” he highlighted.

“Carlos was an important political actor, attractive for his citizen profile. PAN, PRI and Movimiento Ciudadano sought him out, but his essence and that of his voters was related to the left,” he concluded.


After break up with Morena in 2024Carlos Manzo, known as “The One with the Hat”became the first independent Mayor of Uruapan, Michoacánand his frontal stance against organized crime earned him the recognition of his community… and death.

The Government of Manzo, who was shot to death by organized crime on November 1 at a public event for the Day of the Dead, where moments before he had interacted with his children, was marked by controversial actions, as he not only got involved in security operations in person, but he even hit State security elements, accusing them of abuse of authority.

With its municipal government, the capture of one of the commanders of the Jalisco New Generation Cartel (CJNG), “El Rhino”and repeatedly called on the Federation for help to end the violence in Uruapan.

That is, he took actions against crime that contrasted with the alleged passivity of the Governor of Michoacán, the Morenoist Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, whom he accused of being corrupt, stealing and extorting.

At the beginning of April, for example, the theft of a high-end truck in Uruapan provoked a police mobilization in which the man himself participated. Manzo aboard a helicopter, to follow up on the persecution that extended to a rural area of ​​the Caltzontzin community.

“There it is, there it goes down, give it, give it!, here it comes, squeeze it“Manzo was heard saying in a recording made from the air.

At least two shots were then heard from the aircraft towards the stolen truck.
After the chase by land and air, authorities caught the carjacker and recovered a Mercedes Benz truck that had been violently stolen in Uruapan.

A month later and after the murder of a worker from the Uruapan City Council, outside a private school, Manzo instructed the Municipal Police to “shoot down” armed criminals if they resisted arrest or attacked the population.

“The policy of ‘hugs, not bullets’‘it’s over.

You have to put a lot of fire, a lot of force into it to annihilate, to put an end to the entire threat.“, he launched in his speeches.

“Criminals who are found to be armed and who resist arrest or who attack citizens, we must kill them, we must not have any consideration with them (…) We are not going to agree with any criminal group“.

Their statements were disapproved by President Claudia Sheinbaum; However, Manzo responded to the President that If he managed to pacify the municipality “without a shot” he would present his resignation and leave satisfied.

Manzo maintained that Uruapan was “surrounded” by criminal groups that lived by extorting producers, merchants and transporters.

“We were inherited criminal groups that are in all the hills, of all colors, of all the cartels, we are surrounded by criminal groups that are dedicated to extorting and killing.“, he expressed.

His moment of greatest tension came late August, when the Municipal Police arrested René Belmonte Aguilar, “El Rhino”, designated as the CJNG’s plaza boss.

Manzo activated code red, asked the population to protect themselves and demanded urgent support from the Federation.

“At this moment they are reporting to us that armed people are being mobilized to enter Uruapan… We ask that you take shelter until security conditions exist to lift this red code“he warned.

The episode confirmed its frontal collision strategy and its dependence on state and federal reinforcements to maintain control of the territory after blows to criminal commanders.

At the end of September, an officer from the Uruapan Municipal Police was injured in a new attack on elements of the corporation, so Manzo went out on patrol with a bulletproof vest in search of those responsible.

That month, the Mayor asked Sheinbaum for help again.

“If order is not put here in Uruapan, soon at the national level we will hear a strong uprising, of voice, of justice, and if necessary, even of weapons, because people are already fed up“he warned.

His “cleanup” bet involved captures that moved the local board – like that of “The Rhino” – but also increasing risks for himself and his team.

On the night of November 1, 2025, during the Candle Festival in the main square, an attacker approached him and shot him several times.

The federal government confirmed that, despite having protection, the hitmen took advantage of the vulnerability of a massive event.

The Mayor, who feared for his life, assured that citizens would continue fighting crime even if he was not there.

“They may screw me, but they are left with a very angry tiger that is the people of Uruapan. Waters, waters, because if they touch us they will touch the entire town of Uruapan“.

Authorities believe organized crime involved in Mexican mayor’s assassination carried out by teen

Seven mayors have been killed in Michoacan during the past three years
Eduardo Verdugo
,
Fabiola Sanchez
Thursday 06 November 2025 18:35 GMT
Breaking News
For free real time breaking news alerts sent straight to your inbox sign up to our breaking news emails
Email
*

Following the murder of popular Uruapan Mayor Carlos Alberto Manzo, state authorities linked his brutal killing to organized crime.

The teenage attacker who carried out the assassination was a known methamphetamine addict and was shot and killed by the mayor’s security detail.

Michoacan state prosecutor Carlos Torres Piña named the gunman as 17-year-old Víctor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales, who was shot and killed by the mayor’s security detail.

Without providing further detail, Torres Piña said at a news conference on Thursday that more than two people were involved and the attack was tied to organized crime, Torres Piña said at a news conference on Thursday.

Investigators have said the gun used to kill Manzo has been linked to two earlier armed clashes between rival organized crime groups operating in Michoacan.
Casket for Mayor Carlos Alberto Manzo
Casket for Mayor Carlos Alberto Manzo (AP)

Manzo was shot Saturday night in the town’s historic center in front of dozens of people gathered for Day of the Dead festivities. Manzo was hit seven times and died later at a hospital.

Manzo’s wife assumed his position as mayor on Wednesday.

Seven mayors have been killed in Michoacan during the past three years. Mayors are especially vulnerable to organized crime groups in Mexico that seek to control territory to move drugs and extort residents and businesses.

In recent months, Manzo had publicly appealed to Mexico President Claudia Sheinbaum on social media for help to confront the cartels and criminal groups.

Last month, Michoacan was shaken by the killing of a popular and outspoken leader of lime growers, who also suffered extortion from the cartels.

During the last few years, the Mexican federal government has sent hundreds of troops to Michoacan but it hasn’t been enough to control the cells of the Jalisco New Generation Cartel, the Familia Michoacana and local criminal organizations that operate in the state. The state’s persistent violence has resisted interventions from successive administrations.
The body of Víctor Manuel “N”, 17 years old, identified as allegedly responsible for the murder of the mayor of Uruapan, Michoacán, Carlos Manzo Rodríguez, was laid to rest last Wednesday in the community of Paracho, after his relatives claimed his remains. The young man lost his life a few minutes after committing the attack against Manzo, which occurred on the night of Saturday, November 1, in the Plaza de los Mártires, located in the center of the city.
LEE: El Custodio: Who is the youtuber accused of murdering three alleged invaders?

Subsequently, the minor’s body was transferred to his old home in Nurio, a town he had left a week before the homicide. His relatives traveled to Morelia, the state capital, to carry out the legal recognition of the body.

The wake in Paracho was carried out discreetly, with the presence of few people who came to accompany the family during mourning. According to statements provided by relatives to the authorities, Víctor had been absent from home a week before the crime.

The minor had drug use, according to the autopsy

Relatives reported that the young man faced substance addiction problems, including amphetamines and marijuana, something that was confirmed in the autopsy, where traces of said drugs were found in his system. This result, according to the experts, could help understand the mental state and context under which the adolescent acted.
Forensic results confirm his participation in the attack

The state prosecutor of Michoacán, Carlos Torres Piña, reported that Víctor Manuel tested positive for sodium rhodizonate, an analysis used to detect gunpowder residue on the hands, which confirmed his direct participation in the six shots that Mayor Carlos Manzo Rodríguez received.

Investigations have established that at least two other people were involved in the homicide. According to the first advances, The State Attorney General’s Office considers that the attack could be related to the operation of organized crime groups in the Uruapan region, an area historically affected by the presence of these organizations.
LEE: Municipal official murdered while leaving her home in Oaxaca
Possible mastermind

Former mayor Carlos Bautista Tafolla declared that the case should not be closed solely with the identification of the young aggressor, because, in his words, “It is not enough to identify the murderer of Carlos Manzo, we must see who the intellectual author was,” referring to the fact that the crime could have been ordered by third parties.
What the law says about the penalty for homicide

Article 320 of the Federal Penal Code establishes that the penalty for the crime of homicide ranges between 30 and 60 years in prison. Nevertheless, Because Victor was a minor, he would not have been prosecuted as an adult. In that case, he would have been tried under the Adolescent Justice System, where The maximum applicable sentence is 5 years, according to current Mexican legislation.

Carlos Manzo: Why was he compared to Nayib Bukele, mayor of Uruapan?
Home /News/Carlos Manzo: Why was he compared to Nayib Bukele, mayor of Uruapan?
SUN/FILE	
Julius Opaschowski
News | November 2, 2025



Carlos Manzo Rodríguez, mayor of Uruapan, Michoacán, earned the nickname “the Mexican Bukele” due to his firm speech against crime and the security policies that he promoted during his administration. His direct style and his insistence on applying a “firm hand” against organized crime made many They will compare him with the president of El Salvador, Nayib Bukele.

From the beginning of his administration, Manzo publicly expressed his position on the insecurity that afflicted Uruapan. In one of his most memorable messages he declared:

    “Criminals who are found who are armed, who resist arrest or who attack citizens… they must be shot down, there must be no consideration for them.”

LEE: Last words of Carlos Manzo before being murdered in front of his family

These words, spoken forcefully, They marked a before and after in the public perception of the president. His message recalled the zero tolerance policies promoted by Bukele in El Salvador, where the president waged a frontal war against gangs.

SUN/FILE
Security actions

During his government, Carlos Manzo implemented visible measures to reinforce local security. Destination more than 50 million pesos to acquire patrols and armored vehicles, in addition to promoting incentives for municipal agents, with the purpose of strengthening the corporation and promoting honest work in accordance with the law.

These actions, along with his direct style, reinforced the comparison with Nayib Bukele, whose administration is also characterized by its focus on police equipment, territorial control and the visible presence of the State in the streets.

The origin of the nickname “the Mexican Bukele”

The media and citizens began to refer to Manzo as “the Mexican Bukele” due to the similarities in their speech and their way of governing. However, He himself came to distance himself from that label.

“I am not the Mexican Bukele, but I am 100 percent the Michoacan hat,” he stated in an interview, highlighting his local identity and his commitment to the population of Uruapan.

Despite his refusal to compare himself with the Salvadoran president, the similarity in his narrative and his political decisions made him a unique figure within the municipal panorama in Mexico.
A controversial and popular leadership

Manzo came to power as independent candidate, a decision that allowed it to maintain autonomy from political parties. His management was recognized by a part of the population who saw in him a determined leader, willing to face violence with determination. However, it also generated criticism for its rhetoric considered excessively harsh.
LEE: “I am very afraid”: the warning of the mayor of Uruapan before being murdered

His tragic death, which occurred during a celebration in the main square of Uruapan, shocked the country and left an administration that had captured national attention on hold. The figure of Carlos Manzo remains associated with his bravery, his direct way of governing and the inevitable comparisons with Nayib Bukele, the Salvadoran president who transformed the concept of “iron fist” into a leadership style.

HARFUCH ENCUENTRA a CARLOS MANZO en TÚNELES SECRETOS de URUAPÁN… ¿REALIDAD o FICCIÓN?

Famous Story
HARFUCH REVELA el ÚLTIMO MENSAJE que Carlos Manzo RECIBIÓ MINUTOS antes de M*RIR: “Vamos a por ti”
Photo of Diep Tran Diep Tran3 hours ago
1,180 5 minutes read

La noche en que asesinaron a Carlos Manzo ya es una cicatriz profunda en la historia reciente de Uruapan. Lo que no sabíamos, hasta hoy, es que él mismo dejó un mensaje que cambia por completo la dimensión de este crimen y que convierte este asesinato no solo en una ejecución, sino en un desafío directo al Estado mexicano.

Ese mensaje apareció el 16 de noviembre dentro de su propio teléfono, en una conversación de WhatsApp que se había mantenido oculta incluso para la mayoría de los investigadores. Y hoy, como Omar García Harfuch, puedo contar en primera persona qué decía, cómo lo encontramos y por qué su contenido revela que Carlos Manzo sabía que ya no había camino de regreso.

La escena oficial es conocida. Noche del primero de noviembre, festival de velas en pleno centro de Uruapan. Familias, niños, música, papel picado, una plaza convertida en mar de luz. Y en medio de esa celebración, un alcalde que cae frente a todos.

Un joven de apenas 19 años, drogado, armado y entrenado como un soldado desechable, se abre paso entre la multitud. Dispara en menos de cuatro segundos. Y todo lo que era fiesta se convierte en un campo de pánico.

Lo identificamos como Osvaldo Gutiérrez Vázquez, alias “El Cuate”, miembro de una célula del Cártel Jalisco Nueva Generación, con vínculos directos con operadores de alto nivel en la región de Tierra Caliente.

Pero lo que encontramos después, dos semanas más tarde, trastocó absolutamente todo.

Mientras los peritos revisaban el teléfono de Manzo como parte de la investigación complementaria, hubo un chat que destacó de inmediato. Un grupo etiquetado como Seguridad Confidencial. Y dentro de él, a las 19:43 del primero de noviembre, el alcalde escribió las cuatro palabras que hoy son prueba clave:

“Ya vienen por mí.”

No era un comentario al aire. No era paranoia. Era un aviso directo, enviado a personas de su máxima confianza, minutos antes de subir al escenario y enfrentarse cara a cara con su destino.

Y aun así decidió no cancelar el evento.

Ese mensaje, recuperado el 16 de noviembre, confirma que Carlos Manzo sabía que algo grave iba a ocurrir. Que entendió las señales. Y que, aun con miedo, eligió estar frente a su gente.

Porque él no era un político improvisado. Tenía 46 años. Venía de abajo. Había sido comerciante, abogado, vecino de toda la vida en la colonia La Mora. Un alcalde que saludaba por nombre al panadero y que, en solo diez meses de gobierno, rompió contratos turbios, cerró rutas criminales y ordenó operativos que incomodaron a quienes se creían dueños del territorio.

Las amenazas habían crecido durante semanas.

Recados, mensajes, advertencias veladas. Cambios sospechosos en la policía municipal. Presiones para permitir empresas fachada. Exigencias de tolerancia en ciertas rutas.

Carlos se negó una y otra vez.

Y no lo hizo por valentía arrogante, sino por convicción. En reuniones reservadas repetía una frase que ahora duele leer:
“Si cedo una vez, cedí para siempre.”

Aquel “Ya vienen por mí” no era un grito, era la conclusión de un proceso que llevaba meses escalando.

Mientras la banda afinaba instrumentos y las velas iluminaban la plaza, un hombre escribía en su WhatsApp la frase más dolorosamente lúcida de su vida.

Las cámaras del C4 lo muestran minutos después. Sonríe. Saluda. Sube al escenario. Nada en su rostro delata que sabía que el tiempo había comenzado a correr en su contra.

Por eso el mensaje lo cambia todo.

No fue impulsivo. No fue azaroso. No fue un ataque aislado de un joven armado.

Fue una ejecución planificada con calma, con logística precisa, con un objetivo político directo. Y con la intención clara de mandar un mensaje de poder.

Cuando los peritos hallaron el chat completo el 16 de noviembre, lo imprimí en papel. No por desconfianza en lo digital, sino porque ciertos mensajes se entienden mejor como documentos históricos. Y este lo es.

La conversación empezaba muchas horas antes.

Al mediodía, Manzo escribió:

“Traigo información rara. Carros sin placas desde anoche. Al tiro.”

Nadie lo tomó a la ligera. Sus mandos respondieron de inmediato. Revisaban cámaras. Activaban apoyos. Recomendaban reducir apariciones públicas.

Manzo se negó.
“Si me encierro hoy, ellos ganan.”

A las 17:00 llegó otro mensaje inquietante.

“Caras nuevas en el centro. Mochilas grandes. No son del barrio.”

En una ciudad donde todos se conocen, dos desconocidos pueden significar un ataque. Los agentes enviaron fotos, cerraron calles, pidieron revisiones discretas.

El ambiente se tensó minuto tras minuto.

Y a las 19:41 llegó la confirmación de sus escoltas:

“Dos sujetos no son de aquí. Gorra, sudadera negra. Están cerca del kiosco.”

Un minuto después:

“Estamos moviendo unidades.”

Y a las 19:43, la frase que partiría en dos esta investigación:

“Ya vienen por mí.”

Sin signos. Sin dramatismo. Sin despedidas.

Solo certeza.

Un minuto después, otro mensaje suyo:
“No quiero que corran. Que quede registrado.”

Esa línea es un testamento político. Un hombre destinado a morir dando instrucciones para evitar una estampida de pánico.

Al mismo tiempo, muy lejos de Uruapan, otra conversación ocurría. Una célula del CJNG esperaba la señal. Un jefe dio la orden:

“Ya está la música. Ya está la gente. Denle cuando se pare al frente.”

La frialdad contrastaba brutalmente con la serenidad de Manzo.

El ataque estaba sincronizado. No había improvisación. No había dudas.

El cuate avanzó entre la multitud. Un segundo joven saboteó el sistema de sonido para generar confusión. Y cuando el micrófono falló, la plaza quedó desprotegida.

La investigación llevó al siguiente nivel: El Prángana, operador local, reclutador de jóvenes y enlace directo con los hermanos Álvarez Ayala, conocidos como R1 y R2. Los verdaderos coordinadores.

La ejecución de Manzo no fue local. Fue ordenada desde arriba.

Las antenas telefónicas registraron comunicaciones inusuales. Las cámaras captaron vehículos que salieron en sincronía. Y el arma usada por el Cuate coincidía balísticamente con homicidios previos vinculados a esa misma célula.

Cada pieza apuntaba a la misma estructura.

Mientras tanto, Uruapan se sumió en silencio.

Tiendas cerrando antes de tiempo. Calles desiertas. Altares convertidos en memoriales permanentes. Y una frase repetida en testimonios ciudadanos:

“A ese chavo lo trajeron solo a matar. Alguien muy arriba dio la orden.”

La familia de Manzo escuchó el chat completo. Su esposa, Grecia, pidió solo una cosa:

“Que no lo borren. Que quede en la carpeta. Él avisó.”

Y tiene razón.

Ese mensaje no es solo prueba. Es la voz final de un hombre que intentó sostener su responsabilidad hasta el último minuto.

Por eso esta investigación ya no se trata únicamente de capturar al gatillero. Se trata de escalar hasta quienes firmaron la orden. Hasta quienes permitieron que un cártel se sintiera capaz de matar a un alcalde frente a familias, niños y cámaras.

Porque este crimen no fue un ataque contra un hombre.
Fue un ataque contra una institución.

Y mientras esa plaza sigue cubierta de flores, alguien escribió una frase en una cartulina:

“A los que matan a la luz del día, ¿quién los protege en la oscuridad?”

Esa es la pregunta que guía cada paso de esta investigación.

Y es la razón por la que la muerte de Carlos Manzo no será enterrada en silencio.

Carlos Manzo: They ask to participate in tribute to the murdered mayor of Uruapan
Home /News/Carlos Manzo: They ask to participate in tribute to the murdered mayor of Uruapan
Julius Opaschowski
News | November 8, 2025



The case of the murdered mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, continues to move and it was recently announced that the city council itself is preparing a tribute for the politician. What is it about?

The Municipal Government of Uruapan invited the population to donate keys to create a monument in honor of Carlos Alberto Manzo Rodríguezmunicipal president of this city, who was assassinated on November 1 when the Candle Festival was inaugurated.

Through its social networks, the government announced the “Not one step back” campaign and informed the population that The keys will be received at the offices of the House of Culture, located in the Historic Center, in front of the Municipal Pergola.

Review Why does the mayor of Uruapan ask for a punishment vote in 2027?

“Each key you give is a symbol of love, gratitude and hope. From Uruapan hands will be born the monument that will forever remember a man who dedicated his life to serving, to building, to dreaming of a more just and humane Uruapan. Let’s forge his legacy together”.
“Don’t leave me alone”

Yesterday, Grecia Quiroz García left the house of culture with her husband’s hat in her hand and went on stage under a strong security device. The independent mayor was flanked by her escorts dressed in suits, by elements of the National Guard and the Army, and by her family.

With her gaze fixed on two paintings of her husband, she said: “Today, at this moment, Carlos Manzo is standing here next to me, and I want to tell you that This fight will not be in vain. “They may have taken away our leader, but they left us a hero for whom we are going to fight and honor his memory.”.
Lee: Very cold days are coming for Guadalajara; This is how it will be today Saturday

Amongst applause, the new mayor of that municipality located 110 kilometers from the capital of Michoacán, who was wearing a combination of black and white, stated that Today one of Carlos Manzo’s legacies is fulfilled: seeing his people united by this fight, which he defended until the last day of his life..

Grecia, who at times seemed fearful, changed her mood when she heard from the thousands of attendees who accompanied her, the cry of “You are not alone”.

“Today I come to tell you that there is hope for Uruapan, for Michoacán, for Mexico; for all those people who have lost a loved one, for all those who have been extorted, robbed, abused. Today I want to give you that message of hope.”.
Consultation: Experts warn that very cold days are coming for Guadalajara

Quiroz García recalled that the day a 17-year-old teenager shot her husband, she could only pick up his hat from the floor.. “But those who ordered Carlos Manzo to be killed did not know that this hat has an unstoppable and tireless force. Today I also come to tell you that they would have to come and kill us all so that this fight stops walking in the streets and stops supporting the most vulnerable people.”

As the seconds passed, the mayor’s words rose in tone in that unread message for her people, for the political class and for criminals.
“We are not going to let anyone come to trample on the people of Uruguay.”. We are not going to let anyone come and bloody the people of Uruguay even more, we are not going to allow it. Let’s continue walking with the independent movement of the hat. “I need your help, I need you not to leave me alone.”.

Carlos Manzo: Uruapan Prosecutor’s Office officials will be fired
Home /News/Carlos Manzo: Uruapan Prosecutor’s Office officials will be fired
Julius Opaschowski
News | November 17, 2025



This Monday, internal sources of the Michoacán Attorney General’s Office revealed to a national media outlet that, as part of the “cleaning operation“from the state agency, security officials from the town of Uruapanwhere he ruled Carlos Manzo, They would be removed from their positions.

These actions will be carried out within that Regional Prosecutor’s Office this week. So far, it is known that the following have been removed:

    Fiscal regional
    Experts
    Elements that served as the Public Ministry
    Investigation agents
    Secretaries

Read also: 48 arrested after protests by Generation Z in Guadalajara

This measure responds to the events that occurred on November 1, where Carlos Manzo died, shot to death during the Candle Festivaland intends to strengthen operations and research in that area.

It is expected that over the course of the next 48 hours, the Attorney General Carlos Torres Piña make the official announcement about this “cleaning operation” in that Regional Prosecutor’s Office.

Until the end of writing this note, it is unknown when personnel chosen by the same owner will arrive.

Michoacán Plan for Peace and Justice

Last Sunday, November 9, as a measure in response to the assassination of Carlos Manzo, the President Claudia Sheinbaum presented the Michoacán Plan for Peace and Justicea strategy that seeks to bring a state of security for the Western entity.

This proposal was made jointly by the members of the Security Cabinet and the communities of Michoacán.

The axes of this strategy, presented by the head of the Secretary of Security and Citizen Protection (SSPC), Omar García Harfuchwere:

    Security and justicewhich is based on attention to accusations and coordination between security bodies
    Economic development with justice
    Education and culture for peace

HARFUCH ENCUENTRA a CARLOS MANZO en TÚNELES SECRETOS de URUAPÁN… ¿REALIDAD o FICCIÓN?
