Home/Famous Story/Harfuch REVELA el VIDEO donde BEDOLLA HUM*LLA a Carlos Manzo antes de entregarlo
Famous Story
Harfuch REVELA el VIDEO donde BEDOLLA HUM*LLA a Carlos Manzo antes de entregarlo
Photo of Diep Tran Diep Tran2 days ago
5,128 4 minutes read

El país se detuvo por un instante cuando Omar García Harfuch pidió la palabra en la sesión extraordinaria del Senado.
Nadie sabía exactamente qué iba a mostrar, pero el tono de su voz dejó claro que no era cualquier cosa.
Lo que vino después es uno de los registros más oscuros y brutales que se hayan expuesto en la historia reciente de Michoacán.

Un video de 2 minutos 48 segundos.
Una cámara oculta.
Un despacho cerrado.
Un gobernador.
Un activista.
Y una escena que, hasta ayer, muchos se negaban a creer.

Eran las 15:12 del 26 de octubre de 2025.
En la oficina 312 del Palacio de Gobierno estatal, Alfredo Bedolla Maldonado recibió a Carlos Manzo Quiroz, esposo de la alcaldesa de Uruapan, Grecia Quiroz.
Lo que debía ser una reunión sobre seguridad terminó siendo una demostración de abuso de poder, humillación y amenaza directa.

El video comienza con la puerta cerrándose con brusquedad.
Bedolla entra a la habitación sin saludar, sin extender la mano, sin siquiera simular cordialidad.
Camina hacia Manzo, que está sentado frente a un escritorio de madera oscura, y se detiene a menos de un metro de él.

La tensión atraviesa la pantalla.
Se le nota en la respiración de Manzo.
Se le escucha en los silencios.
Y se vuelve contundente cuando el gobernador habla por primera vez.

“Tú y tu mujer se la pasan de listillos, pero aquí se acaba el circo.”
Así, sin preámbulos.
Sin filtro.
Sin diplomacia.

Manzo no contesta.
Sus manos permanecen apretadas sobre la mesa.
Toda la escena se siente como el preludio de algo peor.

Bedolla da un paso adelante.
El dedo índice estirado.
La voz subiendo de volumen:
“¿Crees que no sé lo que andan diciendo por Uruapan?”
Otra pausa.
Y el grito final que retumba en la grabación:
“¡Cállate la boca o te la cierro yo!”

El gobernador golpea la mesa con el puño cerrado.
El estruendo sacude los objetos del escritorio.
Y a partir de ahí el abuso se vuelve evidente, brutal, casi insoportable.

Escupe al suelo.
Ordena a Manzo salir.
Señala hacia la puerta con desprecio.
Pero cuando el activista se pone de pie, dos escoltas entran por la puerta lateral.
Lo toman del brazo.
Lo conducen no hacia la salida principal, sino hacia un pasillo interno del palacio.

Uno de ellos murmura:
“No fue buena idea venir, amigo.”
Y la grabación termina cuando Manzo pisa un estacionamiento trasero de servicio.

Pero ese no es el final.
Es solo el comienzo.

Carlos Manzo llevaba consigo un dispositivo de grabación oculto.
Lo había adquirido semanas antes por miedo.
Por amenazas recibidas.
Por llamadas nocturnas.
Por seguimientos sospechosos.
Y porque la Fiscalía Estatal no había hecho nada para protegerlo.

Encendió el aparato antes de entrar al palacio de gobierno.
Y esa decisión, casi instintiva, se convirtió en la única defensa real que tuvo frente al poder.

Cuando regresó a Uruapan, después de las 7 de la noche, llegó callado.
Distante.
Distinto.
Grecia Quiroz lo notó de inmediato, pero él no dijo nada.
Guardó el silencio.
Guardó el miedo.
Y guardó la grabación.

La copió varias veces.
La encriptó.
La envió a contactos de confianza con la instrucción de hacerla pública si algo le ocurría.
Eso lo hacen las personas que viven en riesgo.
Eso lo hacen quienes saben que el Estado no los protegerá.

El video llegó a manos de inteligencia federal semanas después.
Por canales que no se han revelado.
Pero llegó completo.
Con metadatos intactos.
Con GPS.
Con hora.
Con cada segundo en alta definición.

El análisis fue implacable.
No había cortes.
No había edición.
No había manipulación.
No era deep fake.
Era real.
Absolutamente real.

El Instituto Nacional de Transparencia emitió un dictamen técnico certificando la autenticidad total del archivo.
Ese dictamen tiene peso legal.
Peso judicial.
Y peso político.

Y entonces Harfuch tomó una decisión histórica: mostrarlo en el Senado.
No en una rueda de prensa.
No en una filtración.
En el Senado de la República.
Frente a cámaras.
Frente a legisladores.
Frente al país entero.

Cuando el video terminó de reproducirse, nadie habló durante varios segundos.
El silencio fue tan profundo que parecía un minuto de duelo.
Un duelo por la dignidad pisoteada de un activista.
Un duelo por la evidencia de un gobernador convertido en verdugo político.

Harfuch pidió tres acciones inmediatas.
La primera: que la Fiscalía General de la República abriera investigación por amenazas e intimidación.
Delitos federales.
Delitos documentados.
Delitos innegables.

La segunda: que el Congreso de Michoacán citara a Bedolla a comparecer.
Que diera la cara.
Que explicara lo inexplicable.
Que respondiera por cada gesto de ese video.

La tercera: protección federal para Carlos Manzo y su familia.
Escoltas.
Vigilancia.
Protocolos de seguridad.
Porque el riesgo era real y la amenaza venía desde arriba.

La respuesta del gobernador fue inmediata y predecible.
Aseguró en redes sociales que el video era falso.
Que era un deep fake pagado por opositores.
Que él estaba en un evento público en ese horario.
Pero su propia agenda oficial lo contradijo cinco minutos después.

A las 15:12 no tenía nada público.
Su agenda marcaba “reunión privada sin registro”.
Justo la hora del video.
Justo la oficina.
Justo el lugar.

Grecia Quiroz también habló.
Escribió:
“Ese día Carlos volvió con miedo. Hoy entiendo por qué. En ese video está su dignidad pisoteada.”
Sus palabras desgarraron a todo el país.

Organizaciones civiles convocaron a movilizaciones.
La indignación creció.
La exigencia de justicia también.

Pero para entender este caso hay que ver el contexto completo.
Michoacán lleva años atrapado entre violencia, complicidad y abandono institucional.
Activistas amenazados.
Periodistas perseguidos.
Comunidades extorsionadas.
Gobiernos incapaces de proteger.
O peor: gobiernos que se vuelven parte del mismo mecanismo de intimidación.

Carlos Manzo era una de las pocas voces que se mantenían firmes.
Denunció extorsiones.
Denunció despojos.
Denunció complicidades.
Se enfrentó a poderes que preferían su silencio.

Por eso lo citaron.
Por eso lo encerraron.
Por eso lo humillaron.
Y por eso ese video importa tanto.
Porque documenta el momento exacto en que el poder decidió aplastarlo.

La investigación sigue.
Las presiones aumentan.
Las preguntas crecen.

¿Actuó solo el gobernador?
¿Hubo órdenes superiores?
¿Se trató de una intimidación o de un paso previo a algo peor?
¿A quién más había amenazado antes?
¿Qué otros videos existen?
¿Qué otros abusos permanecen ocultos?

El país quiere respuestas.
Y las quiere ya.

Harfuch cerró su intervención en el Senado con una frase que resonó en todo el recinto:
“México merece funcionarios que sirvan a la ciudadanía, no que la amenacen.”
La frase no fue un cierre político.
Fue un diagnóstico.
Fue una advertencia.
Fue un pedido urgente.

Porque la línea que separa la autoridad del abuso es cada vez más delgada.
Y en Michoacán, ese día, esa línea desapareció por completo.

Carlos Manzo sobrevivió a la reunión.
Pero no salió intacto.
Salió con miedo.
Con rabia.
Con la certeza de que lo querían callar.

Hoy ese silencio se rompió.
Y toda una estructura de poder está temblando.

El video está en manos del país entero.
Y ahora nadie puede fingir que no vio lo que vio.
Nadie puede alegar ignorancia.
Nadie puede decir que no sabía.

Porque desde este momento, México ya no puede mirar hacia otro lado.

Carlos Manzo, Mayor of Uruapan, is assassinated
Home /Opinion/Carlos Manzo, Mayor of Uruapan, is assassinated
Carlos Manzo	
Bailey Craig
Opinion | November 2, 2025


The authorities arrested two people and killed a third after the attack in which the Mayor of Uruapan lost his life.

-Information in development

Mexico City, November 1 (However).- Carlos Manzo, Municipal President of Uruapan, died this Saturday in an attack that occurred in the center of the municipality of Michoacán, reported the Security Cabinet of the Government of Mexico. Two people were arrested and one of the attackers lost his life.

According to the first reports, the Mayor was attacked by gunfire around 8:00 p.m. when he was hanging out with attendees of the Candle Festival, which takes place every year at the Municipal Pergola.

Although the Mayor known as “The One with the Hat” left after lighting the candles, he returned minutes later to take photos with the children dressed in costumes when he was surprised by alleged hitmen who opened fire on him.

After the attack, Carlos Manzo was taken to the Fray Juan de San Miguel Hospital where he finally lost his life due to the impacts. At the scene, the bodyguards managed to kill one of the attackers and subdue two more.

    As a result of an attack that occurred this afternoon in the center of Uruapan, Michoacán, where municipal president Carlos Manzo unfortunately lost his life, two people involved in the events were arrested and one of the attackers lost his life.

Home/Famous Story/El día que las amenazas dejaron de ser palabras: la hija de Carlos Manzo en manos del terror
Famous Story
El día que las amenazas dejaron de ser palabras: la hija de Carlos Manzo en manos del terror
Photo of Diep Tran Diep TranSeptember 15, 2025
3,153 2 minutes read

Cuando la advertencia se hizo realidad: la sombra que cayó sobre Manzo y su hija

El golpe fue certero y planeado con frialdad.
La planilla Independiente de Carlos Manzo en busca de la alcaldía - CENTRAL INFORMATIVA MICHOACÁN

La hija de Carlos Manzo fue privada de su libertad en circunstancias que todavía estremecen.

Lo que comenzó como un rumor se confirmó con la crudeza de la realidad: las amenazas que venían persiguiendo a la familia no eran un simple intento de intimidación, sino una antesala de un crimen anunciado.

Las primeras informaciones hablan de un operativo calculado, con movimientos precisos y sin margen para el error.

Testigos aseguran que todo ocurrió en cuestión de segundos, con una violencia silenciosa que dejó a todos paralizados.
thumbnail

La familia, atrapada entre el pánico y la desesperación, quedó en shock al comprender que el enemigo había cumplido su palabra.

El silencio posterior fue aún más desgarrador.

Las llamadas telefónicas, cargadas de frases cortas y directas, dejaron claro que no había espacio para negociar sin obedecer.

La frialdad de los secuestradores se convirtió en una losa insoportable para Manzo, quien de pronto se vio reducido a un padre desesperado, lejos de cualquier rol público.

Lo que más impacta es la brutalidad del contexto: semanas antes, Carlos había denunciado amenazas contra su vida y la de su familia, advirtiendo que su entorno estaba bajo fuego.
Busca Carlos Manzo, diputado de Morena, senaduría como independiente - Quadratín Michoacán

Muchos lo tomaron como parte de la tensión que lo rodea desde hace años, pero nadie imaginó que los agresores llevarían esas advertencias hasta el límite.

Y ahora, con su hija secuestrada, el mensaje es inequívoco: las palabras ya se transformaron en hechos.

En medio de la tragedia, el ambiente se ha llenado de especulaciones.

Algunos apuntan a rivalidades políticas y otros a venganzas personales.

Sin embargo, lo que todos coinciden es en la saña con la que se ejecutó este golpe.

El secuestro no solo es un ataque contra una familia, sino un mensaje que estremece a cualquiera que ose desafiar a los responsables.
Carlos Manzo no descarta ser encuestado por Morena para gubernatura 2027 - Quadratín Michoacán

Las redes sociales se convirtieron en un hervidero de indignación.

Los seguidores exigen respuestas inmediatas, mientras los detractores utilizan el caso para señalar las consecuencias de los conflictos que Carlos arrastra desde hace años.

Entre tanto ruido, lo único seguro es la angustia de una familia que vive minuto a minuto con la incertidumbre más cruel: ¿está a salvo su hija?, ¿volverá con vida?, ¿qué precio habrá que pagar para que esto termine?

La escena deja una sensación de pesadilla colectiva.

Porque no se trata solo de un secuestro, sino del recordatorio más brutal de que nadie, ni siquiera quienes creen tener control, está a salvo cuando la violencia decide cumplir sus promesas.

Hoy, Carlos Manzo no es político, no es figura pública: es un padre desgarrado, enfrentando el round más oscuro de su vida, con un enemigo invisible que ya demostró que está dispuesto a todo.

Who was Carlos Manzo, the mayor murdered in Mexico that sparked outrage?

Carlos Manzo died as a result of an armed attack in Uruapan, during the Day of the Dead celebration
Who was Carlos Manzo the mayor murdered in Mexico that triggered outrage
Rachna Kumari
Rachna Kumari
Tue, Nov 04 2025 01:21:21 UTC
Time to Read 3 Min

Carlos Manzo Rodriguez was the mayor of Uruapan, Michoacan. He was murdered Saturday night by an assailant during the Day of the Dead celebration in the center of the municipality he governed, where he was with his family.

In Mexico, some people refer to Manzo Rodriguez as the “Mexican Bukele,” referring to his stance against crime, but he rejected that nickname.

“I'm not the Mexican Bukele, but I am 100 percent a Michoacan hat,” he said in an interview published in El Informador in Mexico.

The mayor rose to fame after posting videos on social media where he spoke about his plan to confront crime, mentioning that he had given orders to kill armed criminals who resisted arrest. This sparked criticism against him for possible human rights violations and due process violations, hence the reference to the president of El Salvador, Nayib Bukele.

“If there is a persecution, they must be stopped at all costs,” he said last May, while criticizing human rights organizations: “They don't always do their job well and they don't allow reviews to be carried out.”

Manzo Rodriguez was born on May 9, 1985, in Uruapan, the second largest city in Michoacan; he holds a degree in political science and public administration from the Western Institute of Technology and Higher Education (ITESO), a Jesuit university in Guadalajara, Jalisco.
How did he become mayor?

Manzo Rodriguez was a member of the Institutional Revolutionary Party (PRI), then joined the National Regeneration Movement (Morena) party, which led to his election as a federal deputy.

He was a critic of Felipe Calderon's government and its so-called "war on drugs," led by Genaro Garcia Luna, the former Secretary of Public Security now imprisoned in the US on drug trafficking charges.

"The tragedy began in Michoacan on December 11, 2006, when Felipe Calderon decided to militarize the country, not to provide security for citizens, but to be complicit with the cartels he served."

He said this on the floor of the Chamber of Deputies, where he represented District 09 of Uruapan.

On February 27, 2024, Manzo Rodriguez requested a leave of absence as a federal deputy to run as an independent candidate for mayor of Uruapan, which he won.

Manzo Rodriguez repeatedly requested support from the federal government in Mexico to combat crime in Uruapan, and in June of this year, he acknowledged that there was “coordination” with the administration of President Claudia Sheinbaum, through the Secretary of Security, Omar Garcia Harfuch, to increase security.

However, in mid-October, the mayor stated that 200 National Guard troops had been withdrawn from security duties in the area.

The federal government confirmed that 200 troops had been withdrawn from the area on October 8, but that 100 more arrived on the 18th to reinforce security in Uruapan, with permanent personnel also stationed there.

Tacambaro.
The Mayor's Family

Manzo Rodriguez is survived by his wife, Grecia Quiroz, and two children, one of whom he was holding in his arms when he delivered a message minutes before the attack against him.

Before her husband's coffin in the main square of Uruapan, Grecia Quiroz emphasized that her husband could have been president of Mexico and asked the people to fight against crime.

“Today I tell the people of Uruapan not to give up, to unite, to rise up as he would have liked, to fight, to defend our children tooth and nail, to defend that Uruapan of the past, to defend our country because he would have been the best president of Mexico,” she expressed.

Mexican Mayor Calls for Federal Help After Video Allegedly Shows Cartel Training Camp
Carlos Manzo said multiple criminal groups, including the Jalisco Cartel and Cárteles Unidos, operate in Michoacan
Héctor Ríos Morales Héctor Ríos Morales / Published Jun 20 2025, 8:12 AM EDT

Uruapan training camp
In the video, seven suspected cartel members are seen following instructions from another man during what appears to be a paramilitary-style training session Via Infobae/Carlos Manzo on Facebook

A mayor in the Mexican state of Michoacán is calling for federal assistance to combat organized crime after posting a video that allegedly shows cartel members training at a clandestine camp near the state's border with Jalisco.

Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo said the footage was recovered from a cellphone left behind at a site raided by state authorities. He claimed the video shows a group of armed men undergoing combat-style training.
Related

    Jalisco Cartel Leader 'El Mencho' Slapped With Sanctions For Role In Drug Trafficking And Killings
    Initials of Jalisco New Generation Cartel (CJNG) on Michoacan Wall
    Authorities Reveal New Details in Homicide of Mexican Mayor Investigated Over Ties With Organized Crime
    Martha Laura Mendoza 

In an interview with Infobae México, Manzo said authorities were responding to reports of a kidnapping when they discovered the site. In the video, which Manzo shared on his Facebook page this week, seven suspected cartel members can be seen following instructions from another man during what appears to be a paramilitary-style training session.

"We're starting the day. We've already done the safety checks, right? All right, let's get into some positions so the 'Boss' sees we're not just screwing around and that we're alert," the man recording the video says. He then asks the group to recall its rules.

"Always assume your weapon is loaded before picking it up," the men respond. They are later seen practicing tactical movements and combat stances. "Attack position, combat stance, kneel down, aim, return," the instructor repeats a few times during the video.

Manzo said the footage "shows that there are criminal groups operating paramilitary training camps" in the region. In his post, he also alleged the involvement of Colombian and Venezuelan nationals in camps operating in the Purépecha Plateau region of Uruapan.

"Uruapan is surrounded by criminal groups of every kind, who threaten the safety and social peace of our municipality day after day," he wrote.

Uruapan is located in central Michoacán, less than 60 miles east of the border with Jalisco. The area has long been contested by criminal organizations due to its proximity to key Pacific coast ports used to smuggle precursor chemicals and drugs from China.

Despite the video, Michoacán's public security secretary, Juan Carlos Oseguera Cortés, denied the mayor's claims and said no training camps operated by criminal groups have been identified.

"In the municipality of Uruapan, we are working in coordination with local authorities, and as of today, there is no evidence confirming the presence of any training camps in Michoacán," Oseguera Cortés said.
Need to Know Basis by Latin Times
A newsletter that delivers the news you actually need.
Related

    Colombian Official Confirms At Least One Active Military Member is Working For Mexican Cartels
    Colombian soldiers
    Jalisco New Generation Cartel Becomes First Cartel in History to Have Presence in All 32 Mexican States
    cartel presence states 

Manzo urged Mexican President Claudia Sheinbaum and Security Secretary Omar García Harfuch to intervene and help protect his community. He also sent a direct message to criminal groups to leave Uruapan and stop harming civilians.

"Don't abandon Uruapan. Do whatever is necessary so that honest, hardworking people are no longer harmed by kidnappings, homicides, extortion and vehicle theft," Manzo wrote. "We ask the criminals to stay away from Uruapan and to stop killing innocent people in their turf wars."

The mayor also emphasized that local residents don't care which criminal group is dismantled — only that peace is restored. "We're only asking for peace and security for our people," he said. "I'm making this appeal because the crimes committed by these individuals fall under federal jurisdiction, and it is the responsibility of the federal government to address this issue directly."

Murder of Carlos Manzo woke up the sleeping tiger: Guadalupe Mendoza
Home /News/Murder of Carlos Manzo woke up the sleeping tiger: Guadalupe Mendoza
The independent representative Guadalupe Araceli Mendoza Arias, of the Sombrero Movement, remembered the murdered mayor Carlos Manzo in San Lázaro.	
Julius Opaschowski
News | November 11, 2025


The independent federal representative Guadalupe Araceli Mendoza Ariaswho is part of the Hat Movementwhich was led by the murdered mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo.

He stated in the plenary session of Saint Lazarus who intended to kill the legacy of the next governor of Michoacan and future president of Mexico, his way of working aroused jealousy and envy of popularity in criminal organizations, politicians or adversaries, but they awakened the “sleeping tiger, the roaring tiger.”

You may also be interested in: Sedena denies failure of the security protocol in the murder of Carlos Manzo

    “The easiest thing was to have him eliminated, to remove him from the map, but they got a big surprise, first, by turning Carlos Manzo into a national and international hero and waking up the sleeping tiger, as he said so often, that tiger that roars for thirst for justice and for true transformation. Now they woke up the Mexicans, they wanted to kill the legacy that he would be the next governor of Michoacán and future president of Mexico,” he exclaimed.

    🔴 Independent representative Guadalupe Mendoza paid tribute to Carlos Manzo, mayor of Uruapan. He recalled his work in the Hat Movement and stated that his death “awakened the sleeping tiger.” pic.twitter.com/3sFtqS1Y8w

    — Azucena Uresti (@azucenau) November 11, 2025

He highlighted that the people received Carlos Manzo the strength, courage and awareness of how they wanted to be governed through security, peace, with tranquility and confidence to have a better world.

The independent representative sent a clear message to those who have the power to say goodbye to luxuries, deals and corruption.

    “Little by little, say goodbye to the luxuries of power, the dealings and the corruption that clearly shines, because now it is up to us, those of the hat movement, to support that legacy, that fight with his wife Grecia Quiroz, who heads this great movement,” he warned.

He asked the mayor for support Uruapan, Michoacán, Greece Quirozand stressed that the hat is not an accessory, it is an ideal.

    “Long live the best president of Mexico, Carlos Manzo! Long live the sombreriza! Long live Mexico! and we will not take a step back, not a step back and no step back, because we will continue working no matter who it is,” he exclaimed.

Guadalupe Mendoza highlighted the achievements of Carlos Manzo

Guadalupe Araceli Mendoza Arias highlighted that Carlos Manzo He had potential as a human being and social leader, he attended to health issues through his free hat pharmacies and his citizen service table where he responded to thousands of citizens.

He also formed a group of volunteers called: The Citizen Hat Guardwith which he fought against the police and traffic corporations, which were dedicated to robbing and extorting citizens, especially at the entrances and exits of Uruapan.
The media reports that the murderer of Carlos Manzo Rodríguez, mayor of Uruapan, Michoacán, has already been identified.
Darkroom |

So, like doing conferences, where they distributed pantries, backpacks, toys, food, as snacks in the most vulnerable neighborhoods of the city. The surveillance patrols, works that were transparent, without corruption and always giving everything for others.

    “In the year 2024, he seeks the mayoralty of the city of Uruapan, defeating his competition with a historic vote in the municipality, also obtaining two local deputies and one federal one, which is the one that I lead,” he pointed out.

You may also be interested in: Carlos Manzo’s escorts will continue to testify and are not detained, says Harfuch

    “A year and months after the independent government, together, those of the hat, we achieved more throughout the district, managing the resource with all transparency, where apart from our salary as deputies we added to this effort, thus being a way of responding to those who gave us their trust at the polls and projecting our movement at the national level, even awakening sympathies at the international level,” he added.

HARFUCH ENCUENTRA a CARLOS MANZO en TÚNELES SECRETOS de URUAPÁN… ¿REALIDAD o FICCIÓN?

Home/Famous Story/Carlos Manzo: El Alcalde que Enfrentó al Cárt*l — y Pagó con su Vida
Famous Story
Carlos Manzo: El Alcalde que Enfrentó al Cárt*l — y Pagó con su Vida
Photo of Diep Tran Diep Tran2 days ago
94 4 minutes read

La madrugada todavía no despertaba cuando el país entero entendió que algo había cambiado para siempre.
A las 3:18 de la mañana, una operación silenciosa, quirúrgica y brutal reveló lo que muchos sospechaban, pero nadie se atrevía a decir en voz alta.
El asesinato del alcalde Carlos Manzo no fue un ataque aislado.
Fue un mensaje.
Un desafío directo al Estado mexicano.

Y fue también el inicio de una guerra.

Dicen que hay un momento antes de Carlos Manzo y otro después de él.
Porque Manzo no era un político más.
Era alguien que se paró frente al poder criminal y lo señaló con nombre y apellido.
Alguien que denunció lo que otros callaban por miedo.

Y por eso lo mataron.

Lo ejecutaron en medio del festival de las velas, frente a su gente, frente a su ciudad.
Los disparos no iban solo contra su cuerpo.
Iban contra la idea de que en Michoacán aún había autoridades dispuestas a defender a su pueblo.
La violencia fue rápida, precisa, humillante.

Pero lo peor vino después.

A menos de una semana de su muerte, su viuda, Grecia Quiroz, recibió una amenaza directa.
El mensaje llegó desde un número desconocido, en la noche, cuando el silencio hace más daño.
Le dijeron que iban por ella, por sus hijos, por la madre del propio Manzo.
No era una advertencia.
Era una sentencia.

La familia del alcalde tuvo que huir.
No por política.
Por venganza.

Y mientras tanto, puertas adentro, en los pasillos del poder, comenzó a moverse una versión que pocos querían ver salir a la luz.
Un video filtrado.
Una reunión.
Un grupo de hombres que jamás debieron estar en la misma habitación.

En la grabación, fechada a finales de junio, aparece Carlos Manzo sentado frente a varios nombres del ámbito político y mediático.
Entre ellos, personajes que públicamente lo condenaban, pero que en privado lo buscaban.
El video dura pocos minutos.
Pero lo suficiente para poner en jaque a todos.

Porque en la cinta se escucha claramente cómo Manzo describe amenazas, movimientos criminales y pactos que estaban pudriendo las instituciones desde dentro.
Él sabía demasiado.
Y aún así habló.

Ese fue su error, dicen algunos.
Ese fue su valor, dicen otros.

Lo cierto es que su muerte no detuvo nada.
Solo lo aceleró.

Tras la ejecución del alcalde, se desató una guerra interna por el control de Uruapan y sus alrededores.
Una guerra que comenzó con una operación a las 4:45 de la madrugada, bajo lluvia helada, cuando un convoy de fuerzas especiales irrumpió en un punto que las autoridades llamaban “El Corazón”.
El corazón del problema.
El corazón del cártel.

Esa operación secreta, que debía permanecer oculta, se filtró en cuestión de horas.
Como si alguien quisiera asegurarse de que todos supieran que el Estado ya no tenía el control del silencio.
Y las consecuencias fueron inmediatas.

Los grupos criminales respondieron con fuego.
Con amenazas.
Con mensajes que dejaban claro que si el gobierno entraba, ellos no iban a retroceder.

Pero lo más polémico no fue la violencia.
Fue la pregunta que comenzó a repetirse por todo México.

¿Quién dejó solo a Carlos Manzo?

Porque él denunció directamente a la Guardia Civil.
Denunció al gobernador.
Denunció la corrupción que, según él, estaba asfixiando al estado desde dentro.
Dijo que lo querían callar.
Que lo querían dominar.
Que no simpatizaba con sus políticas corruptas.

Y terminó muerto.

Su asesinato fue una declaración.
Un aviso a todos los que se atrevieran a levantar la voz.

Pero también fue el inicio de algo más grande.
Una investigación que empezó con periodistas locales y que rápidamente escaló a agencias federales y contactos internacionales.
Porque los reportes del mundo criminal no mentían.
Había un pacto.
Había una red.
Y Carlos Manzo estaba en medio.

Lo que realmente ocurrió la noche en que lo mataron no está completamente claro.
Y quizás nunca lo estará.
Pero las piezas que han salido a la luz forman un rompecabezas demasiado perfecto para ser coincidencia.

Un político incómodo.
Un gobierno molesto con él.
Un cártel que lo quería fuera.
Una familia amenazada.
Un pueblo aterrado.

Y un video.
Un video que podría hundir carreras enteras si llegara a hacerse público en su versión completa.

Los habitantes de Uruapan dicen que Manzo sabía que lo iban a matar.
Dicen que sus últimas semanas fueron un desfile de advertencias disfrazadas de rumores.
Que tenía miedo, pero que nunca se escondió.

Dicen que murió como vivió:
confrontando.

Hoy, su ciudad vive con la herida abierta.
Las velas del festival siguen encendiéndose cada año.
Pero ya no iluminan celebración.
Iluminan memoria.

La muerte de Carlos Manzo no terminó con él.
Desató alianzas nuevas.
Rompió silencios viejos.
Y encendió una rabia que ya no se puede apagar.

En los pasillos políticos se murmura que vienen más revelaciones.
Que el caso apenas empieza.
Que hay nombres que aún no se han dicho.
Y que algunos de los implicados tienen nervios de acero para negar todo…
y otros no tanto.

Pero en las calles, donde está la gente que lo vio nacer, gobernar y morir, la historia es distinta.
La pregunta que repiten no es “¿quién lo mató?”
Esa ya la saben.

La pregunta real es:

¿Quién lo entregó?

Porque esa es la pieza que nadie quiere soltar.
La pieza que podría derribar todo un sistema.

Carlos Manzo se convirtió en símbolo.
En mártir.
En la evidencia viva —y ahora muerta— de que aún hay alcaldes que prefieren enfrentar al cártel antes que pactar con él.

Y por eso pagó con su vida.

Pero su historia no terminó esa noche.
Sigue escribiéndose en cada filtración.
En cada testimonio.
En cada operativo inexplicable.
En cada silencio incómodo del gobierno.

Y mientras más tiempo pasa, más clara se vuelve una verdad que todos intentaron esconder:

Carlos Manzo no cayó por azar.
Cayó porque representaba un problema para demasiados.
Y ahora, muerto, sigue siéndolo.

Famous Story
Harfuch revela el video prohibido de la esposa de Carlos Manzo
Photo of Diep Tran Diep Tran2 days ago
11,390 5 minutes read

Lo primero que se escucha no es un grito. Es un murmullo. Un susurro que se multiplica en la penumbra.

Como si el aire supiera algo. Como si alguien lo hubiera visto todo. Pero nadie se atreve a decirlo en voz alta.

Si el video existe, ¿quién lo grabó? ¿Quién lo guardó? ¿Y por qué aparece justo ahora?

Cuando las preguntas sobre la muerte de Carlos Manzo incomodan a demasiados. Cuando el país se divide entre la esperanza y el miedo. Cuando el apellido Harfuch se pronuncia como una llave y un cerrojo al mismo tiempo.

La promesa es brutal. Un video filtrado. Una viuda convertida en símbolo.

Una traición que, si es cierta, reescribe lo ocurrido esa noche en Uruapan. Y si es falsa, entonces alguien está fabricando sombras para esconder una verdad más grande.

Antes de hablar del video, hay que mirar lo que desató la tormenta. Carlos Manzo, alcalde de Uruapan, cayó en plena celebración de las velas. La multitud, el papel picado, los puestos, la música.

Nadie imagina la fractura hasta que la escucha. Lo que sucede después no cabe en la palabra casualidad. Al día siguiente, la seguridad federal admite que el atacante murió.

Que hubo más manos. Que la investigación apunta a organizaciones que se mueven como niebla y cuchillo. No lo dice cualquiera.

Lo dice quien desde seguridad asume la escena del crimen como su prueba más visible. Las autoridades identifican al agresor. Hablan de participación del crimen organizado.

El caso estalla. Se vuelve nacional en menos de lo que dura un rezo. Ahí comienza el otro relato.

Redes desbocadas. Clips sin contexto. Títulos que no avisan, que prometen.

Surge la frase que incendia los chats. Harfuch filtró el video. La afirmación no se sostiene en documentos oficiales.

No hay rueda de prensa que lo confirme. Lo que sí existe es un vacío. Y en medio del vacío, la necesidad de colgar un hecho de un rostro conocido.

En política de seguridad, el silencio es una grieta. Por ahí se cuela la versión más útil para quien quiera manipular el ánimo público. Quien entendió eso, lo supo de inmediato.

El relato no es la realidad. Pero si domina la conversación, la condiciona. Michoacán es una prueba de fuego para la estrategia federal.

No es detalle menor. Cualquier imagen, cierta o no, puede torcer la percepción. ¿Existe el video?

Aquí la verdad es incómoda. Hay publicaciones virales que juran lo indescriptible. Hablan de una pieza de menos de un minuto.

Una escena interpretada como traición. Lo sostienen páginas que viven de la atención. Influencias digitales que monetizan un encabezado.

Pero no hay confirmación oficial. No hay peritaje público. No hay expediente que lo acredite.

Lo que sí está claro es el contexto. El asesinato ocurrió en una fiesta tradicional. El agresor fue identificado como menor de edad.

Vinculado al consumo de sustancias. La Fiscalía Estatal habló de más participantes. Lo comprobable por ahora es eso.

Lo demás es humo. Entonces, ¿por qué un país entero mira una supuesta filtración como si pudiera explicar lo inexplicable? Porque la palabra traición, junto a la palabra viuda, abre un abismo moral.

La rabia busca caer ahí. Cuando asesinan a una figura que se enfrentaba a poderes oscuros, el dolor pide culpables. Adicionales, secundarios, tangenciales.

Y en momentos de luto, la intimidad de los deudos se vuelve rehén. La pregunta clave no es qué muestra el video. Sino quién gana si tú crees haberlo visto.

Carlos Manzo había pedido respaldo para enfrentar a los grupos criminales. Su muerte desató marchas. Reclamos al gobernador.

Exigencias de justicia. La respuesta institucional admitió que el atacante no actuó solo. Que el arma estaba vinculada a otros hechos violentos.

Todo eso alimentó la noción de una conspiración. Más grande que un tirador joven. Más grande que una bala.

Las agencias internacionales trazaron ese mapa mínimo de certezas. Un crimen. Un sospechoso abatido.

La insinuación de complicidades. Una familia que pasa del duelo a la lucha cívica. ¿Dónde encaja el supuesto video?

En el punto exacto donde el dolor choca con la propaganda. Las narrativas en redes no necesitan documentos. Necesitan emociones.

Si alguien te dice que hay un video filtrado por Harfuch, está invocando la idea de un poder capaz de todo. Incluso de exponer la intimidad de una mujer para fabricar una verdad conveniente. Esa imagen condena sin juicio.

Tritura sin evidencia. Dirige la furia hacia el círculo más cercano al muerto. Ahora respiremos.

¿Qué sí dijo Harfuch de manera verificable? Dijo que el agresor murió a manos de los escoltas. Que había protección federal para el alcalde.

Que se investigaba la red detrás del ataque. El presunto tirador era un joven identificado por la fiscalía. El arma tenía historial.

En ninguna declaración aparece la admisión de haber filtrado material íntimo. No hay conferencia. No hay boletín.

No hay cita directa. Lo que sí hay son comunicados registrados. En ellos, el énfasis es la cadena de responsabilidades criminales.

No una guerra sucia contra la viuda. Si el video no está acreditado, ¿por qué su sombra crece? Porque la historia oficial avanza a ritmo de expediente.

La historia emotiva viaja en segundos. Los algoritmos favorecen lo que nos agita. El duelo público hace el resto.

Todo conspira para que un título incendiario dicte la conversación. La trampa está servida. Quien controla el rumor, controla el tiempo.

Y en un país fatigado por la violencia, el rumor es alivio y veneno. Lo que sí es verificable es que tras el atentado, la viuda se convirtió en figura pública. Asumió responsabilidades.

Se plantó frente a un estado cuestionado. En situaciones así, la familia ocupa el lugar más luminoso y más cruel. La esperanza y la carne viva.

Cualquier imagen impacta en la legitimidad de esa voz. Cuando un material aparece en el peor momento, casi nunca es casualidad. Es una operación de desgaste.

Una manera de convertir a quien pide justicia en objeto de juicio. Que algunos contenidos intenten vincular su nombre con la palabra traición no significa que haya pruebas. Significa que hay intención.

Y cuando hay intención sin evidencia, hay manipulación. Las crónicas serias siguen el rastro de los hechos. Las balas, las rutas, los vínculos.

Los mandos medios. La mano que aprieta el gatillo. La mente que paga por ese gatillo.

Aquí la historia gira. Imagina la noche de la tragedia como un tablero apagado. De pronto recibe una luz intermitente.

Cámaras urbanas. Teléfonos ciudadanos. Transmisiones breves.

Los investigadores no buscan escándalos domésticos. Buscan coordenadas. Temporización.

Ángulos. Rutas de escape. Dispositivos conectados.

Si un video íntimo aparece, no ilumina la escena del crimen. Distrae de ella. Pone a la audiencia a discutir moralidades.

En lugar de exigir responsabilidades penales. Esa es la geometría del distractor. ¿Y qué hay de la versión opuesta?

La que susurra que la filtración proviene de una oficina pública. La historia mexicana conoce episodios oscuros. Espionaje, filtraciones, campañas de lodo.

Pero si se acusa, se demuestra. No hubo documento oficial. No hubo carpeta abierta por filtración.

No hubo citatorio que imputara a funcionarios federales. Lo que sí hubo fueron ruedas de prensa. Hablaban de la autoría material.

Los posibles nexos. La ruta del arma. La estrategia de seguridad bajo la lupa.

La pista institucional fue otra. ¿Quién se beneficia de que el duelo cambie de tema? El crimen organizado.

Quien compite en política. Quienes monetizan la indignación. Un rumor bien escrito puede vender más que una carpeta bien armada.

Un titular con la palabra traición puede borrar problemas más pesados. Como la cadena de mando que permitió que un menor fuera sicario. Como la pregunta que nadie quiere contestar.

November 4, 2025
Mexico
1 min read
Widow of Carlos Manzo is preparing to take her husband’s place in the mayor’s office of Uruapan
Widow of Carlos Manzo is preparing to take her husband's place in the mayor's office of Uruapan

Grecia Quiroz affirmed that the legacy of her husband Carlos Manzo will remain, as well as his fight against organized crime.

When giving a speech during the posthumous tribute to Manzo, held in the main square of that city of Michoacán, she assured that she and the citizens will continue working against injustices.

“Today they did not kill the president of Uruapan, they killed the best (municipal) president in Mexico, the only one who dared to raise his voice, who dared to debate, to speak the truth, to always tell the truth, without fear of anything.

“As his brother said so well: although they turned off his voice, they will not turn off this fight, they will not turn it off because we will continue his legacy,” he said.
Carlos Manzo was laid to rest on Sunday, November 2 in Michoacán.
(Photo: Cuartoscuro)

Manzo, 40, was shot and killed Saturday while attending a candle festival at a Day of the Dead celebration in downtown Uruapan.

Two suspects were arrested and a third was killed, the Ministry of Public Security reported on Saturday.

Manzo, one of the few elected independent politicians in Mexico, was mayor of Uruapan since September of last year.

Since taking office, Manzo, who was frequently seen wearing a bulletproof vest, had called on the federal government to step up the fight against organized crime, while expressing fear for his own safety.

Uruapan is known as the Mexican avocado capital because it is located in the heart of the avocado-producing region in Michoacán.

The industry has experienced rapid growth due to increasing demand in the United States, which has made avocado production a target for organized crime groups.

The mayor had asked President Claudia Sheinbaum for stronger public safety measures and had stated that Uruapan’s avocado industry gave it importance in the face of the upcoming review of Mexico’s trade agreement with the United States and Canada.

Manzo had also expressed that greater determination was required on the part of the Secretary of Security, Omar Harfuch. “Secretary Omar Harfuch, serve us,” Manzo said in that interview.

In a press conference on Sunday, Harfuch stated that Manzo had federal protection since December 2024, which was reinforced in May.

Protection included 14 National Guard troops charged with perimeter security, while local police provided immediate security.

-With information from Reuters.

Mexican mayor who spoke out against cartels shot to death

by RAY LEWIS | The National News DeskMon, November 3, 2025 at 4:52 PM
Updated Mon, November 3, 2025 at 4:58 PM
GettyImages-2235654404.jpg
The Mexican flag flies in Mexico City on Sept. 15.Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo was shot to death on Saturday during an event in his city. (Photo by Hector Vivas/Getty Images)

    topics:
    Mexican mayor
    Carlos Manzo
    Uruapan
    Cartels
    Assassination
    Michoacán
    Security
    Impunity

HUNT VALLEY, Md. (TNND) — A Mexican mayor who spoke out against cartels was shot to death at a Day of the Dead event on Saturday.

Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo, who had urged the federal government to fight crime differently, was killed during a candlelight ceremony in the southwestern city. President Claudia Sheinbaum and Michoacán Gov. Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, whose state includes Uruapan, have denounced the attack.

“I condemn with absolute firmness the vile assassination of the municipal president of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo,” Sheinbaum said in a translated social media post. “I express my most sincere condolences to his family and loved ones, as well as to the people of Uruapan in the face of this irreparable loss.”

Bedolla called the shooting “cowardly” and expressed sympathy for Manzo’s family.

“I know that his murder generates tremendous rage and indignation; we are all dismayed and outraged, but we are going to step up and act immediately to ensure that there is justice and peace for the people of Uruapan,” he wrote in a translated X post.

The alleged attacker was killed at the scene, Bedolla noted. Two people associated with the incident were also taken into custody, according to the governor. He spoke about Manzo’s death with Sheinbaum, who also convened the security cabinet to ensure support for Michoacán and that there won’t be any “impunity.”

“From the start of this administration, we have strengthened the Security Strategy. These such regrettable events drive us to strengthen it even further,” Sheinbaum added, referencing her administration’s security policies. “We reaffirm our commitment to devote all the efforts of the State to achieve peace and security with zero impunity and justice.”

Have questions, concerns or tips? Send them to Ray at rjlewis@sbgtv.com.

Carlos Manzo talked about not becoming another Mexican mayor who gets executed months before being killed at Day of the Dead event
Story by Aaratrika Bal
• 2w • 3 min read

On November 1, 2025, Mexican mayor Carlos Manzo was shot dead during Day of the Dead celebrations in Michoacán. According to reports by NPR, the incident took place in front of dozens of people who had assembled there for the festivities. Manzo was known for being outspoken about tough laws to deal with drug cartels.

The incident happened just over a month after Manzo said that he didn't want to be just another Mexican mayor who got executed. In September, while speaking to local media, Carlos Manzo said,

    "We need greater determination from the president of Mexico. I do not want to be just another mayor on the list of those who have been executed and had their lives taken away from them. I am very afraid, but I must face it with courage."

Mexican police kill 13 in shootout with suspected cartel members
Story by Zach Kaplan
• 1w • 2 min read
Mexican police kill 13 in shootout with suspected cartel members

(NewsNation) — Thirteen suspected drug cartel members were killed during a shootout with police in the Mexican state of Sinaloa on Monday.

Security Minister Omar Garcia Harfuch announced in a social media post that in addition to the 13 killed, four people involved in the shootout were detained, and nine others who had been kidnapped were freed.

Garcia Harfuch said that the shootout took place after Mexican authorities were “attacked by an armed group hidden under a bridge.” He also confirmed that several vehicles, weapons and tactical equipment were secured following the shootout.

The state, home to the infamous Sinaloa cartel, has experienced a large amount of violence over the past year between factions of the cartel and authorities as they attempt to take back control of the area, as reported by Reuters.
What to know about Trump and rising tensions with Venezuela
Trump eager to stop flow of illegal drugs to U.S.

Since starting his second term, President Donald Trump has made it a priority to stop the flow of illegal drugs into the U.S. from Mexico and other Latin American countries.

In February of this year, the Department of State officially designated the Sinaloa cartel, along with seven other Latin American gangs, as “Foreign Terrorist Organizations.”

“It is one of the world’s most powerful drug cartels and is one of the largest producers and traffickers of fentanyl and other illicit drugs to the United States. Cártel de Sinaloa has used violence to murder, kidnap, and intimidate civilians, government officials, and journalists,” the Department of State press release reads.

Apatzingán burns after the murder of Carlos Manzo
Home /Opinion/Apatzingán burns after the murder of Carlos Manzo
Bailey Craig
Opinion | November 4, 2025


The death of Carlos Manzo unleashed a wave of protests that show the security crisis in Michoacán and the pressure on the state government.

Mexico City, November 3 (However).- Protesters They set fire to and vandalized the Municipal Palace of Apatzingan, Michoacanduring a series of protests in the entity for the murder of the Mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzoand of lemon leader, Bernardo Bravo. The mobilization took place this Monday with the demand for justice and security in the region.

According to reports, the dissatisfied group advanced through the main streets of Apatzingán until reaching the Municipal Palace, where they broke doors, windows and entered the interior of the building. building. On the ground floor of the building, the protesters caused a fire which spread rapidly through several workshops.

During the events, the participants hung a blanket on the main balcony to demand the resignation of Mayor Fanny Arreola Pichardo, a Morena activist. In addition, they destroyed offerings and decorations alluding to the Day of the Dead that were installed in the central plaza.

As the demonstration progressed, the protesters raised slogans against Governor Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, whom they accused of not guaranteeing the safety of the mayors and community leaders of Michoacán. With this, the protest turned violent when a group began throwing objects and furniture from the balconies of the building.

    #Apatzingan is not left behind in marching asking for justice for #CarlosManzo pic.twitter.com/tucCk9aE6n

    — CARLOS SÁNCHEZ 🧜🏼‍♂️ (@Adrielsaor) November 4, 2025

Local authorities and firefighters went to the scene to put out the flames, although the protesters resumed the fire on the first floor of the building minutes later. The incident caused severe structural damage and loss of administrative documents.
Michoacán marches after the crime of Carlos Manzo

More than two thousand students marched this Monday through the main avenues of Uruapan, Michoacán, to demand justice for the murder of Mayor Carlos Manzo Rodríguez and demand an end to violence in the entity. The mobilization began on Lázaro Cárdenas Avenue, known as the old track, and moved towards the center of the city.

    The participants carried banners, white t-shirts and black bows as a symbol of mourning. Among the most repeated slogans was: “Carlos did not die, the Government killed him!”, reflecting the social discontent after the homicide that occurred last weekend.

According to local media, the murder of the Mayor was the trigger for a series of disagreements accumulated due to the insecurity experienced by the communities of Michoacán. The protesters assured that their demand is not limited to clarifying the crime, but rather seeks to promote an environment of peace and security throughout the state.

    Students of Uruapan have just taken control of the streets due to the death of Mayor Carlos Manzo, student strike in the coming days until justice is done

    👌Mexico is already getting up, it has already taken off the blindfold

    Damn those who defend brunette‼️🤬 pic.twitter.com/ha0YjFDKNP

    — ☘ DonRafa🇲🇽 #MexicoLibertario (@Rafagais) November 3, 2025

Alberto Jiménez, student representative in Uruapan, pointed out that the young people came out afraid, but determined to raise their voices. He explained that marching in Michoacán implies a risk, although it is necessary to make visible the situation of violence that affects the population.

The march included the participation of students from the Lázaro Cárdenas University, the Michoacana University of San Nicolás de Hidalgo and other public and private institutions. During the day, some schools suspended classes in support of the movement.

In nearby communities, such as Paracho, San Juan Parangaricutiro and Tancítaro, student strikes were also reported in solidarity with the Uruapan protest. In addition, residents of rural areas blocked the Uruapan-Los Reyes highway to demand the arrest of those intellectually and materially responsible for the crime.

Likewise, an additional demonstration was called in Morelia for this afternoon, where students from at least nine institutions plan to replicate the demand for justice and security. With this, local authorities estimated that the mobilizations will continue during the week, if there is no progress in the investigation.

    🚨🚨🚨Uruapan -Michoacán-

    Students march pic.twitter.com/oiBwdRbOBr

    — Eco_1_LVM (@Eco1_LVM) November 3, 2025

The Governor of Michoacán, Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, recognized the legitimacy of the protests and stated that his Administration is working to clarify Manzo’s murder: “There is indignation and pain, but also a commitment to act.”
Carlos Manzo asked for help before his murder

Carlos Manzo, Municipal President of Uruapan, Michoacán, has long denounced the situation of violence that the community is experiencing and even asked the Government of President Claudia Sheinbaum Pardo for help to combat organized crime. On November 1, the Mayor was shot dead at a public event.

Several videos circulate on social networks that captured the exact moment in which the Mayor is shot dead during the Candle Festival, held on the esplanade of the Inmaculada of said town. These recordings show the moments of terror and confusion that were experienced after the attack.

A couple of months ago, in September, the Municipal President of Uruapan shared a video on social networks to make an urgent call to President Sheinbaum and the federal government with the aim of requesting the support of federal forces to combat organized crime.

The Michoacan mayor also urged the head of the Secretariat of Security and Citizen Protection (SSPC)Omar García Harfuch, to visit his municipality to learn first-hand about the situation of violence.

Carlos Manzo insisted that it is the responsibility of the federal authorities to combat organized crime and warned that if the federal government did not reinforce security, the population of Uruapan would be exposed to being victims of crime.

Months after denouncing the violent situation in Michoacán and requesting the support of President Sheinbaum, the Mayor of Uruapan was shot dead during a public event held on Saturday, November 1.

Several videos are circulating on social networks that captured the moments of terror that people witnessed after the attack against the Mayor, which were recorded by the people present at the scene of the events.

Mexican mayor killed after urging for tougher cartel stance
0

Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo, who had publicly urged Mexico's leaders to take a tougher stance on cartels, was gunned down on Saturday during a Day of the Dead ceremony in Uruapan, Michoacán, state officials said. He was shot seven times; one suspected attacker was killed, and two others were detained.

The assassination is just the latest of violent incidents around Michoacán, a state described by The Wall Street Journal as the hub of Mexico's avocado industry and a long-time battleground for cartels that extort growers.

Straight Arrow News (English)
Mexican mayor killed after urging for tougher cartel stance
0
View on WatchView on Watch

Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo, who had publicly urged Mexico's leaders to take a tougher stance on cartels, was gunned down on Saturday during a Day of the Dead ceremony in Uruapan, Michoacán, state officials said. He was shot seven times; one suspected attacker was killed, and two others were detained.

The assassination is just the latest of violent incidents around Michoacán, a state described by The Wall Street Journal as the hub of Mexico's avocado industry and a long-time battleground for cartels that extort growers.
What Manzo argued about fighting cartels

Manzo had been a vocal critic of Mexico's national security strategy. In September, he told local media, "We need greater determination from the president of Mexico," and vowed not to take "a single step back," Fox News reported.

He openly acknowledged the danger, saying, "I do not want to be just another mayor on the list … I am very afraid, but I must face it with courage."

He told The Wall Street Journal that he personally led police operations to "preach by example" and urged federal forces to "clean the mountains of the people who are killing and extorting avocado growers."

World News
2 journalists killed in separate incidents in Mexico within 24 hours
Updated 10:49 PM CST, October 30, 2024

MEXICO CITY (AP) — The U.N. human rights office in Mexico said Wednesday journalists in Mexico need more protection, after gunmen killed a man whose Facebook news page covered the violent western Mexico state of Michoacan.

Then less than 24 hours later an entertainment reporter in the western city of Colima was killed inside a restaurant she owned.

Journalist Mauricio Solís of the news page Minuto por Minuto was shot to death late Tuesday just moments after he conducted a sidewalk interview with the mayor of the city of Uruapan (ooh-roo-WAH-pan). State prosecutors said a second person was wounded in the shooting.

Solís had just finished an interview on the street outside city hall with Mayor Carlos Manzo. Manzo told local media he had walked away and “two minutes later, I think, and just a matter of meters away, we heard gunshots, four or five gunshots.”

“We sought cover because we thought the attack was aimed at us,” Manzo said. “After a few minutes we found out that Mauricio was the one they attacked.”

Manzo said he could not rule out a connection between the interview and the killing.

The U.N. rights office said Solís was at least the fifth journalist killed in Mexico this year. It said he had previously reported security problems related to his work. His Facebook page reported on community events and the drug cartel violence that has wracked the city.
Related Stories
Organized crime believed involved in killing of popular Mexican mayor by teenage gunman
Organized crime believed involved in killing of popular Mexican mayor by teenage gunman
Colombian President Petro suggests Qatar could mediate US military actions off Venezuela
Colombian President Petro suggests Qatar could mediate US military actions off Venezuela
Mexico to send more troops and money to Michoacan after mayor's killing
Mexico to send more troops and money to Michoacan after mayor's killing

“His killing is a wake-up call to defend the right to information and freedom of expression in Mexico,” the office wrote.

An increasing number of the journalists killed in Mexico have been self-employed and reported for local Facebook and online news sites.

Uruapan is the nearest large city to Michoacan’s avocado-growing region, and it has been the scene of drug cartel extortions and turf battles between gangs. The cartels demand protection money from local avocado and lime orchards, cattle ranches and almost any other business.

Solís was reporting on a suspicious fire at a local market just before the shooting. Gangs have sometimes burned businesses that refuse to pay extortion demands.

Then on Wednesday afternoon, entertainment reporter Patricia Ramírez González was found with serious injuries inside her Colima restaurant and died at the scene, according to the Colima state prosecutor’s office.

Local media said Ramírez, who was better known as Paty Bunbury, published a blog on local entertainment and was a contributor to a Colima newspaper.

The U.S.-based Committee to Protect Journalists condemned both killings and called for transparent investigations.

Власти Бизнес Силовики Криминал Культура События
Protests in Mexico City saw violent clashes erupting after the assassination of anti-cartel Mayor Carlos Manzo
23:12, 17 ноября 2025 г.
1701     0
Protests in Mexico City saw violent clashes erupting after the assassination of anti-cartel Mayor Carlos Manzo
Protests in Mexico City saw violent clashes erupting after the assassination of anti-cartel Mayor Carlos Manzo

The unrest followed the early November killing of anti-cartel Mayor Carlos Manzo, as protesters denounced the government’s response to his assassination and demanded better security across the country. It comes as the latest in a global wave of youth-led anti-corruption movements.

Thousands of people marched through Mexico City on Saturday to protest rising cartel violence and government corruption, following the early November murder of anti-crime mayor Carlos Manzo. The protests took place in 50 cities across 30 states, according to local reports.

Wearing sombreros and carrying banners calling for justice for Manzo, demonstrators gathered to commemorate the late mayor, who was killed by a teenager allegedly recruited by the Jalisco New Generation Cartel (CJNG) during a Día de los Muertos celebration on November 1. Manzo, who was mayor of the cartel-dominated city of Uruapan, was known for his hard-line stance on cartels. Prior to his assassination, he had reportedly appealed to the federal and state governments for protection.

The march began peacefully but later erupted into clashes between police and protesters, leaving 120 people injured and resulting in 20 arrests, according to Mexico City security chief Pablo Vázquez. He added that most of the injured were police officers, including 40 who required hospital treatment.

According to local media, the clashes broke out near the National Palace, which had been barricaded. Some protesters reportedly knocked down metal barriers and confronted police guarding the building.

Vázquez also said that the demonstrations had remained peaceful until “hooded individuals began to carry out violent acts,” prompting authorities to increase police presence. He said the group responded by “throwing explosive devices” at officers.

President Claudia Sheinbaum dismissed the size of the protests during an event in Tabasco state on Saturday, saying that “very few young people” had participated and accusing some demonstrators of “violently removing barriers and breaking windows.” She addressed the clashes saying, “We say no to violence.”

The conservative National Action Party (PAN) issued a statement condemning what it called “the state’s violent response against the young demonstrators.” Mexico’s Supreme Court of Justice also denounced the violence against police and the “attempts at unauthorized and violent entry into the building.”

The protests in Mexico are part of a broader global wave of youth-led anti-corruption movements. Beginning in August in Indonesia and Nepal, the demonstrations have since spread to seven other countries—including the Philippines, Morocco, Madagascar, Togo, and Peru—where young people have mobilized against systemic corruption, inequality, and impunity. Despite being organized under the banner of “Gen Z,” Mexico’s protests drew thousands of participants of all ages, not only youth.

Michoacán confirms that Carlos Manzo’s murderer was 17 years old
Home /Opinion/Michoacán confirms that Carlos Manzo’s murderer was 17 years old
On Wednesday, Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, took office as substitute Mayor of Uruapan.	
Bailey Craig
Opinion | November 6, 2025


The State Prosecutor’s Office confirmed that the murderer of the Mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo, was a minor; He said that more than 2 people participated in the homicide.

–Information in development

Mexico City, November 6 (However).– The State Attorney General’s Office (FGE) of Michoacan reported this Thursday that confirmed the identity of the autor material of the murder of the Mayor of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo: this is a 17 year old young man resident of the municipality of Paracho, Victor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales. The authorities also stressed that in the homicide participated “more than two people” and is related “to groups of the organized crime“.

    “On the afternoon of November 5, the body of the perpetrator of this homicide was identified and claimed. He is Víctor Manuel Ubaldo Vidales, 17 years old, originally from and resident of the municipality of Paracho, Michoacán,” reported the Prosecutor of Michoacán, Carlos Torres Piña, in a video published on social networks.

“Víctor Manuel’s family recognized that he was absent from home a week before the events. His identification allows us to continue advancing in this investigation, in its context and possible more participants. It is important to reiterate that the expert opinions of the body, confirming the hypothesis of material authorship, as well as his addictions to methamphetamine, information ratified by his relatives,” added.

On Wednesday, Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, took office as substitute Mayor of Uruapan.
On Wednesday, Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, took office as substitute Mayor of Uruapan. Photo: Rogelio Morales

Víctor Manuel’s body was handed over to his relatives for burial.

    In addition, the Prosecutor of Michoacán confirmed that, through intelligence work, “more than two people participated in the murder of Carlos Manzo” and reiterated that the homicide “is related to organized crime groups”, in particular the Jalisco New Generation Cartel (CJNG).

“The investigation work is maintained in a coordinated manner between federal and state authorities. We appreciate the support and support of Secretary Omar García Harfuch, as well as his team. This fact will not go unpunished,” concluded the Prosecutor of Michoacán.
What is the case of the murder of Carlos Manzo going?

Prosecutor Torres Piña highlighted in an interview with The Financier that one of the lines of investigation considers the possible connection between the murder of Municipal President Carlos Manzo and the recent arrest of René Belmonte Aguilar, alias “El Rino”, designated as the regional leader of the cartel, by elements of the municipal police of Uruapan.

However, he added that no hypothesis has been ruled out and that all lines of investigation remain open.

And the official explained that the weapon used in the homicide of Carlos Manzo is related to two previous attacks committed in that same city, which reinforces the line of investigation that points to the CJNG as the alleged perpetrator.

The Prosecutor detailed that the first attack occurred on October 16, when two people were murdered, while the second took place on October 23 in a bar, where one victim lost his life and another was injured. In both cases, the victims were allegedly linked to a rival organization of the CJNG.

He also told the newspaper that the 14 elements of the National Guard assigned to escort Carlos Manzo, as well as the eight municipal police officers in charge of his close security, have already testified before the Prosecutor’s Office.
Widow Grecia Quiroz assumes her husband’s position in Uruapan
Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, took over as Mayor of Uruapan to complete her husband's term until 2027. Photo: Rogelio Morales, CuartoscuroGrecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, took over as Mayor of Uruapan to complete her husband's term until 2027. Photo: Rogelio Morales, Cuartoscuro
Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, took over as Mayor of Uruapan to complete her husband’s term until 2027. Photo: Rogelio Morales, Cuartoscuro

Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo, Mayor of Uruapan murdered last Saturday, took office to complete her husband’s term of government, which ends in 2027. The Municipal Council elected her unanimously and the Congress of Michoacán respected the decision.

The Cabildo is made up of members of the Hat Movement, founded by Carlos Manzo. The Governor of Michoacán, Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, confirmed that they would respect the decision he made about the successor, which ended up being Quiroz, since that political force is the one that had triumphed in Uruapan in 2024.

Michoacán Prosecutor’s Office reports the disappearance of Óscar Sergio Vivanco Romano, following the assassination of Carlos Manzo
Written by Parriva — November 12, 2025

Relatives of a man identified as Óscar Sergio Vivanco Romano reported his disappearance to the State Attorney General’s Office (FGE).

The victim became known on social media for his constant criticism of the Uruapan municipal government, specifically targeting the late mayor, Carlos Manzo.

On November 10, the institution issued a missing person alert for Óscar Sergio, 50 years old, who, according to the description of events, was last seen on November 8, 2025, at approximately 1:50 p.m., on the Ziracuaretiro-Caracha highway in Michoacán.

On his social media accounts, Vivanco Romano frequently uploaded videos criticizing the actions of the authorities and Carlos Manzo as mayor of Uruapan.

In one of the posts, he even issued a threat against councilman Víctor Hugo de la Cruz, known as “Víctor Saladitas,” who was injured during the attack on the murdered mayor. Other posts he shared on his Facebook account include videos of confrontations, and another is related to esoteric practices.

The Michoacán Attorney General’s Office detailed that Óscar Sergio is 1.70 meters tall, weighs 112 kilograms, has a robust build and fair complexion; he has a round face, a broad forehead, shaved head, medium-sized brown eyes, and slightly arched eyebrows.

Among his distinguishing features are scars on his abdomen and both legs, as well as tattoos on his hands: on the right, the image of Anubis, and on the left, a skull along with the names “Lucía, Óscar, Charly, and Nicole.”

On the day of his disappearance, he was wearing gray and black sweatpants, a navy blue t-shirt with navy blue lettering and the number 22, and navy blue sandals.

The Attorney General’s Office requests the public’s support in providing any information that may help locate him.

Who is Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo who demands justice
Home /News/Who is Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo who demands justice
Julius Opaschowski
News | November 3, 2025



After the murder of Carlos Manzo, mayor of Uruapan, which occurred on Saturday, November 1 during a public event on the occasion of the Day of the Dead, Grecia Quiroz, the mayor’s wife, issued a message in which she highlighted her fight and assured that she will continue with his legacy.
Who is Grecia Quiroz, widow of Carlos Manzo?

Grecia Itzel Quiroz García, like her husband, entered the political life of Michoacán. Although her personal information—beyond the family with two children that she formed with Manzo—is not in the public domain, it is known that in 2024 she sought to be a local representative for district 20 of Uruapan Sur.
You may be interested: Harfuch rules out evidence of links between Manzo’s bodyguards and organized crime

Currently, Quiroz serves as honorary president of the Municipal DIF of Uruapan. In this position, the widow is in charge of managing support for vulnerable groups in the town. After receiving the appointment directly from her husband, Grecia accompanied him in recent months at various public events to benefit the people of Uruapan.

Grecia Quiroz and her children were at the place where Carlos Manzo was shot dead on the night of Saturday, November 1. After the attack, the mayor was taken to a hospital; however, he died from gunshot wounds.
Check out: This is what Carlos Manzo’s complaints were like before his murder

During the posthumous tribute held on the afternoon of Sunday, November 2 in the main square of the city, Quiroz García tearfully asked Manzo’s followers to defend his legacy “tooth and nail”:

“Today I tell the people of Uruapan that we do not falter, that we unite, that we rise up as he (Manzo) would have liked; that we fight, that we defend our children tooth and nail, that we defend that Uruapan of before, that we defend our homeland, because he would have been the best president of Mexico”he said before the coffin.

Likewise, she assured that she will continue with the independent organization that her husband promoted, known as the Hat Movement.

“Today I thank all the people who are gathered here, because I know that these people always supported him, at all times: since we collected the signatures, since we walked in the streets to ask for his support, a support that was to change many things that he wanted, but that today truncated that path. But, as his brother said, although they turned off his light, they will not turn off this fight… We will continue fighting together with the Hat Movement,” he expressed to those present.

Carlos Manzo talked about not becoming another Mexican mayor who gets executed months before being killed at Day of the Dead event
Story by Aaratrika Bal
• 2w • 3 min read
WASHINGTON, DC - MARCH 12: Caution tape hangs as members of the Metropolitan Police Department investigate a shooting between two cars at the 400 block of 11th Street SE, on Sunday, March 12, 2023. One male was pronounced dead at the scene and a second male succumbed to their injuries on the way to the hospital. (Photo by Al Drago for The Washington Post via Getty Images)

WASHINGTON, DC - MARCH 12: Caution tape hangs as members of the Metropolitan Police Department investigate a shooting between two cars at the 400 block of 11th Street SE, on Sunday, March 12, 2023. One male was pronounced dead at the scene and a second male succumbed to their injuries on the way to the hospital. (Photo by Al Drago for The Washington Post via Getty Images)

On November 1, 2025, Mexican mayor Carlos Manzo was shot dead during Day of the Dead celebrations in Michoacán. According to reports by NPR, the incident took place in front of dozens of people who had assembled there for the festivities. Manzo was known for being outspoken about tough laws to deal with drug cartels.

One male was pronounced dead at the scene and a second male succumbed to their injuries on the way to the hospital. (Photo by Al Drago for The Washington Post via Getty Images)

WASHINGTON, DC - MARCH 12: Caution tape hangs as members of the Metropolitan Police Department investigate a shooting between two cars at the 400 block of 11th Street SE, on Sunday, March 12, 2023. One male was pronounced dead at the scene and a second male succumbed to their injuries on the way to the hospital. (Photo by Al Drago for The Washington Post via Getty Images)

On November 1, 2025, Mexican mayor Carlos Manzo was shot dead during Day of the Dead celebrations in Michoacán. According to reports by NPR, the incident took place in front of dozens of people who had assembled there for the festivities. Manzo was known for being outspoken about tough laws to deal with drug cartels.

The incident happened just over a month after Manzo said that he didn't want to be just another Mexican mayor who got executed. In September, while speaking to local media, Carlos Manzo said,

    "We need greater determination from the president of Mexico. I do not want to be just another mayor on the list of those who have been executed and had their lives taken away from them. I am very afraid, but I must face it with courage."

Off-duty pilot who tried to cut a flight's engines midair is released without prison time
Story by Claire Rush
• 3h • 3 min read
Former Alaska Airlines pilot Joseph Emerson, center, walks into U.S. District Court in Portland, Ore., on Monday. ((Molly J. Smith / Associated Press))

A former Alaska Airlines pilot who tried to cut the engines of a passenger flight in 2023 while riding off-duty in the cockpit will serve no additional prison time, a federal judge ruled Monday.

U.S. District Court Judge Amy Baggio sentenced Joseph Emerson to time served and supervised release for three years following a hearing in Portland, Ore. Federal prosecutors had asked for one year in prison, while his attorneys sought probation.

“Pilots are not perfect. They are human,” Baggio said. “They are people and all people need help sometimes.”

Emerson was subdued by the flight crew after trying to cut the engines of a Horizon Air flight from Everett, Wash., to San Francisco on Oct. 22, 2023 while riding in an extra seat in the cockpit. The plane was diverted to Portland, where it landed safely with more than 80 people on board.
Former Alaska Airlines pilot Joseph Emerson, center, walks into U.S. District Court in Portland, Ore., on Monday. ((Molly J. Smith / Associated Press))

A former Alaska Airlines pilot who tried to cut the engines of a passenger flight in 2023 while riding off-duty in the cockpit will serve no additional prison time, a federal judge ruled Monday.

U.S. District Court Judge Amy Baggio sentenced Joseph Emerson to time served and supervised release for three years following a hearing in Portland, Ore. Federal prosecutors had asked for one year in prison, while his attorneys sought probation.

“Pilots are not perfect. They are human,” Baggio said. “They are people and all people need help sometimes.”

Emerson was subdued by the flight crew after trying to cut the engines of a Horizon Air flight from Everett, Wash., to San Francisco on Oct. 22, 2023 while riding in an extra seat in the cockpit. The plane was diverted to Portland, where it landed safely with more than 80 people on board.

After his arrest, Emerson told police he was despondent over a friend’s recent death, had taken psychedelic mushrooms about two days earlier, and hadn’t slept in more than 40 hours. He has said he believed he was dreaming at the time and was trying to wake himself up by grabbing two red handles that would have activated the plane’s fire suppression system and cut off fuel to its engines.

Emerson, of Pleasant Hill, Calif., was charged in federal court with interfering with a flight crew. A state indictment in Oregon separately charged him with 83 counts of endangering another person and one count of endangering an aircraft. He was released from custody pending trial in December 2023, with requirements that he undergo mental health services, stay off drugs and alcohol and keep away from aircraft.

Mexican mayor who spoke out against cartels shot to death

by RAY LEWIS | The National News DeskMon, November 3, 2025 at 1:52 PM
Updated Mon, November 3, 2025 at 1:58 PM
GettyImages-2235654404.jpg
The Mexican flag flies in Mexico City on Sept. 15.Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo was shot to death on Saturday during an event in his city. (Photo by Hector Vivas/Getty Images)

    topics:
    Mexican mayor
    Carlos Manzo
    Uruapan
    Cartels
    Assassination
    Michoacán
    Security
    Impunity

HUNT VALLEY, Md. (TNND) — A Mexican mayor who spoke out against cartels was shot to death at a Day of the Dead event on Saturday.

Uruapan Mayor Carlos Manzo, who had urged the federal government to fight crime differently, was killed during a candlelight ceremony in the southwestern city. President Claudia Sheinbaum and Michoacán Gov. Alfredo Ramírez Bedolla, whose state includes Uruapan, have denounced the attack.

“I condemn with absolute firmness the vile assassination of the municipal president of Uruapan, Carlos Manzo,” Sheinbaum said in a translated social media post. “I express my most sincere condolences to his family and loved ones, as well as to the people of Uruapan in the face of this irreparable loss.”

Bedolla called the shooting “cowardly” and expressed sympathy for Manzo’s family.

“I know that his murder generates tremendous rage and indignation; we are all dismayed and outraged, but we are going to step up and act immediately to ensure that there is justice and peace for the people of Uruapan,” he wrote in a translated X post.

The alleged attacker was killed at the scene, Bedolla noted. Two people associated with the incident were also taken into custody, according to the governor. He spoke about Manzo’s death with Sheinbaum, who also convened the security cabinet to ensure support for Michoacán and that there won’t be any “impunity.”

“From the start of this administration, we have strengthened the Security Strategy. These such regrettable events drive us to strengthen it even further,” Sheinbaum added, referencing her administration’s security policies. “We reaffirm our commitment to devote all the efforts of the State to achieve peace and security with zero impunity and justice.”

Have questions, concerns or tips? Send them to Ray at rjlewis@sbgtv.com.
